وترك العاطف لئلا يشعر بالتبعية فيخل بالتسوية.
ترجمہ ! اور مصنف نے حرف عاطف کو چھوڑ دیا تا کہ وہ تبعیہ کے ساتھ مشعر نہ ہو پس وہ تسویہ میں خلل ڈال دے۔
جواب سوال مقدر۔ سوال ! ہوتا ہے کہ تسمیہ و تحمید جب دونوں حال ہیں تو ان کے درمیان حرف عطف کا ذکر مناسب تھا یوں کہا جاتا فحامد آیا وحامداً کیونکہ جب جملہ حال واقع ہو تو اس میں واو یا ضمیر رابطہ کیلئے ضروری ہیں نیز یہ موقع عطف بھی ہے کیونکہ علم . معانی میں ضابطہ درج ہے کہ حرف عطف وہاں ذکر کیا جاتا ہے جہاں معطوف علیہ و معطوف کے درمیان نہ کمال اتصال ہو نہ کمال انفصال بلکہ من وجه اتصال ومن وجہ انفصال ہو یہاں حمد و تسمیہ میں بھی من وجہ اتصال ومن وجہ اتصال رہے لہذا یہاں حرف عطف مناسب تھا حرف عطف کا ذکر مخل بالمقصود تھا کیونکہ مطلوب مصنف تسویہ بین الحمد والصلوۃ ہے اگر حرف عطف ذکر کیا جاتا تو تسو یہ نہ ہوتا کیونکہ معطوف معطوف علیہ کے تابع ہوتا ہے تو ابتداء بالتسمیہ بالا صالۃ اور ابتداء با الحمد تبعاً ہوتی تو مساوات نہ ہوتی اسی وجہ سے حرف عاطف ترک کر دیا۔
And he omitted the conjunctive particle so that it does not indicate subordination, which would disrupt equality. Translation: The author omitted the conjunctive particle so that it does not indicate subordination, which would create an imbalance in equality. Answer to the supposed question: The question is that when both tasmiah and tahmid are in the accusative case as hal, it would have been appropriate to mention a conjunction between them, e.g., 'fa-hamidan wa hamidan', because when a circumstantial clause occurs, it requires a waw or a pronoun as a connector. Moreover, this is a place for conjunction because the rule in 'ilm al-ma'ani is that the conjunction is mentioned where there is neither complete connection nor complete disconnection between the conjoined items, but connection in one respect and disconnection in another. Here too, there is connection in one respect and disconnection in another, so a conjunction would have been appropriate. However, mentioning the conjunction would have been contrary to the intended purpose because the author's aim is equality between tahmid and tasmiah. If the conjunction were mentioned, the second would be subordinate to the first, so beginning with tasmiah would be primary and beginning with tahmid would be secondary, and equality would not be achieved. For this reason, the conjunctive particle was omitted.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage explains a stylistic choice in the author's formulation. The author deliberately omits the conjunctive waw between 'hamidan' and 'musalliyan' (or 'hamidan' and 'mubashshiran') in the original text. The objection raised is that since both are accusative circumstantials (hal), they should be connected by 'waw' for grammatical consistency and to indicate a nuance of partial connection. The author's response is that using 'waw' would imply subordination (taba'iyya) of the second to the first, which contradicts the intended equality between praising Allah (hamd) and sending blessings (salah). By omitting the conjunction, both are given equal status, as if two independent circumstantials. This illustrates how the Hanafi commentator uses linguistic analysis to justify the author's wording and to preserve the legal nuance of taswiyya (equality).

Key Terms
العاطف (al-atif): The conjunctive particle (waw) that connects two grammatical items.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the author omit the conjunctive waw between 'hamidan' and 'musalliyan'?
A) Due to a grammatical error
B) To indicate that the second is subordinate to the first
C) To preserve the intended equality between hamd and salah
D) Because the two items are completely separate

Key Takeaway
Omitting the conjunctive waw between two circumstantial clauses can be a deliberate stylistic choice to preserve equality and avoid subordination, demonstrating how linguistic decisions carry legal significance in Hanafi usul.

Grammatical Obstacles in Textual Analysis: The Case of 'Hamidan'
Grammatical analysis of 'hamidan' as hal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three grammatical obstacles that prevent a circumstantial accusative (hal) from being governed by a specific verb and explain how variant recensions affect textual interpretation in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Grammatical obstacles like the conjunctive waw and 'inna' can block a hal from its governing verb, but variant recensions remove these barriers.

In Hanafi usul, precise grammatical understanding is indispensable for deriving rulings from sacred texts. This passage examines a subtle grammatical issue: whether the word 'hamidan' (praising) functions as a circumstantial accusative (hal) from the verb 'yaqul' (he says) or from a different implied verb. The analysis reveals how textual variants can alter syntactic relationships, and thus potentially affect legal interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Issue
Understand the question: In the opening of a legal text, is 'hamidan' a hal describing the subject of 'yaqul' (the one who says) or of 'ibtada'a' (the one who begins)? The author argues that in the standard recension, it cannot be from 'yaqul'.
The hal describes the state of the agent at the time of the action.
2
Examine Obstacle 1: The Conjunctive Waw
The phrase begins with 'wa ba'du fa-inna al-'abda'. The waw is a conjunctive particle linking what follows to something preceding. According to Arabic grammar, no part of what is conjoined can precede the conjunction. If 'hamidan' were from 'yaqul', it would be part of the conjoined clause and would have to come after the waw, yet it appears before it. This is impermissible.
The rule: 'الجزء المعطوف لا يتقدم على حرف العطف' (a part of the conjoined cannot precede the conjunctive particle).
3
Examine Obstacles 2 and 3: 'Inna' and Redundancy
Obstacle 2: The particle 'inna' requires that nothing before it act on what follows (muqtaḍā al-ṣadārah). Since 'yaqul' is after 'inna', it cannot govern 'hamidan' which precedes 'inna'. Obstacle 3: The implied mudaf ilayh of 'ba'du' is 'al-hamd wa al-salah', which if made explicit causes repetition and redundancy because 'hamid' already implies praise.
These obstacles are specific to the standard recension's wording.
4
Contrast with the Old Recension
The old recension reads: 'mujalliyan wa musalliyan li-yaqul al-'abdu al-mutawassilu ila Allah'. This version lacks the waw, 'inna', and the implied mudaf ilayh that caused redundancy. Therefore, the three obstacles disappear, and 'hamidan' can correctly be a hal from 'yaqul'.
This demonstrates how textual variants directly impact grammatical analysis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجوز ان يكون حامدا حالا من فاعل يقول لان قوله وبعد فان العبد على مافي النسخة المقروة عند المصنف صارف عن ذلك واما على النسخة القديمة الخالية عن هذا الصارف فالظاهر انه جال عنه.
ترجمہ! اور جائز نہیں ہے کہ حامد اً یقول کے فاعل سے حال بنے کیونکہ مصنف کا قول وبعد فان العبد جیسا کہ نسخہ مقروة عند المصنف میں ہے اس سے مانع ہے اور لیکن نسخہ قدیمہ کے مطابق جو کہ اس مانع سے خالی ہے پس راجح یہ ہے کہ حامداً اُس یقول سے حال ہے۔
جواب سوال مقدر۔ سوال ! ہوتا ہے کہ حامداً کو ابتدا کی ضمیر سے حال بنانے کی بجائے یقول کی ضمیر سے حال بنانا اولی وانسب ہے کیونکہ وہ جزء کتاب ہے جبکہ تسمیہ کا جزء ہونا مشکوک مشتمل ہے اس سے حال کیوں نہیں بنایا گیا۔ جواب انسخہ مقروہ وموجودہ کے مطابق یقول سے حال بنانا صحیح نہیں ہے اور عدم صحت کی تین وجوہ ہیں ۔ وجہ (۱) وبعد فان العبد میں واؤ حرف عطف ہے ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ معطوف کے اجزاء میں سے کوئی جزء حرف عطف پر مقدم نہیں ہوسکتا کیونکہ اس صورت میں حرف عطف کا بین اجزاء المعطوف واقع ہونا لازم آئے گا جو کہ ناجائز ہے مثلا ضربت زیر آوا کرمت عمروا میں ضربت زید عمر وا وا کر مت کہنا درست نہیں ہے اگر حامد کو یقول سے حال بنایا جائے تو یہ معطوف کا جزء ہوگا لہذا اس کی تقدیم علی حرف الواو العاطفہ جائز نہ ہوگی حالانکہ یہاں مقدم ہے۔ وجہ (۲) یہ ہے کہ فان العبد میں ان موجود ہے جو مقتضی صدارت کلام ہے اور اس کے مابعد اجزاء میں سے کوئی جزء ماقبل میں عامل نہیں ہوسکتا ورنہ صدارت فوت ہو جائیگی لہذا لیقول حامدا میں عمل نہیں کر سکتا۔ وجہ (۳) یہ ہے کہ بعد کا مضاف الیہ محذوف منوی ہے وہ الحمد والصلوۃ ہے تو عبارت اس طرح بنے گی و بعد الحمد والصلوة يقول العبد حامد اللہ تعالی اس میں تکرار بلا فائدہ ہے اگر نسخہ قدیمہ کو لوظ رکھا جائے جس کی عبارت اسطرح ہے مجلیا ومصلیا لیقول العبد المتوسل الی اللہ تو حامد اکو لقول سے حال بنانا درست بلکہ راج ہے کیونکہ اس عبارت میں موانع ثلاثہ مرتفع ہیں نہ واؤ ہے نہ ان ہے اور نہ بعد ہے راجح
And it is not permissible for 'hamidan' to be a circumstantial accusative from the agent of 'yaqul' because his saying 'wa ba'du fa-inna al-'abda' according to the recension read in the presence of the author prevents that. However, according to the old recension which lacks this preventer, the apparent is that it is a hal from 'yaqul'. Translation: It is not permissible for 'hamidan' to be a hal from the agent of 'yaqul' because the author's statement 'wa ba'du fa-inna al-'abda' as in the recension read before the author prevents that. But according to the old recension which lacks this preventer, the preferred view is that 'hamidan' is a hal from that 'yaqul'. Answer to the supposed question: The question is that making 'hamidan' a hal from the pronoun of 'ibtida' rather than from 'yaqul' is more appropriate and suitable because it is part of the book, while making it part of tasmiah is questionable. Why is it not made a hal from 'yaqul'? Answer: According to the recited and available recension, making it a hal from 'yaqul' is not correct, and there are three reasons for its incorrectness. Reason (1): In 'wa ba'du fa-inna al-'abda', the waw is a conjunctive particle. The rule is that no part of the conjoined can precede the conjunctive particle. If 'hamidan' is made a hal from 'yaqul', it would be a part of the conjoined, and its precedence over the conjunctive waw would be impermissible. Reason (2): In 'fa-inna al-'abda', there is 'inna' which requires precedence in the sentence, and no part after it can act as an operator in what precedes, otherwise the precedence would be lost. Therefore, 'yaqul' cannot govern 'hamida'. Reason (3): The mudaf ilayh of 'ba'du' is omitted but understood to be 'al-hamd wa al-salah'. Then the phrase becomes 'wa ba'du al-hamd wa al-salah yaqulu al-'abdu hamida Allah ta'ala', which is a repetition without benefit. If the old recension is adopted, which is 'mujalliyan wa musalliyan li-yaqul al-'abdu al-mutawassilu ila Allah', then making 'hamidan' a hal from 'yaqul' is correct, indeed preferred, because in this phrase the three obstacles are removed: there is no waw, no 'inna', and no 'ba'du'.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage engages in a detailed grammatical analysis of the textual variant. The issue is whether 'hamidan' (praising) is a circumstantial accusative (hal) describing the subject of 'yaqul' (he says) or the subject of 'ibtida' (he begins). The author argues that in the standard recension (the one read before the author), it is not from 'yaqul' due to three syntactic obstacles: (1) the waw at the beginning of 'wa ba'du' is a conjunction, and parts of what follows cannot precede it; (2) 'inna' requires that nothing before it acts on what follows; (3) the implied mudaf ilayh of 'ba'du' creates redundancy. However, in a older recension without these obstacles, 'hamidan' can be a hal from 'yaqul'. This illustrates how variant readings affect grammatical analysis and consequently, the interpretation of the text.

Key Terms
الحال (al-hal): A circumstantial accusative describing the state of the agent or object at the time of the action.
العاطف (al-ʿāṭif): The conjunctive particle (like waw) that links two elements.
مقتضى الصدارة (muqtaḍā al-ṣadārah): The requirement that certain particles (like 'inna') occupy the first position in their clause, preventing anything before them from governing what follows.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because of a grammatical error
B) Because of the presence of 'wa' and 'inna' which create syntactic obstacles
C) Because 'hamidan' is actually a predicate
D) Because the old recension prohibits it

Key Takeaway
Grammatical obstacles in a text can block syntactic relationships, and variant recensions can resolve them, affecting how a text is interpreted in Hanafi usul.

Three Syntactic Blocks on 'Hāmidan' as a Hāl from 'Yaqūlu'
Explaining why 'حامدا' cannot be a حال from 'يقول' with three reasons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three grammatical reasons preventing 'حامدا' from being a حال from 'يقول' in the standard textual version, and explain how the old version removes these blocks.

Core Idea
Three Arabic syntax rules prevent 'حامدا' as a حال from 'يقول' in the standard version; a textual variant removes them all.

In Usul al-Fiqh, the precise parsing of a single word can alter the interpretation of a legal text. The commentator here examines whether the word 'حامدا' (praising) can be a حال (circumstantial accusative) of the subject of 'يقول' (he says). The answer hinges on which version of the book one follows. This lesson unpacks the three syntactic preventers that forbid this reading in the standard version and contrasts it with an older version where it is not only permitted but preponderant.

Guided Path
1
Identify the grammatical issue
Recognize that 'حامدا' is an accusative of state (حال). The question is whether it describes the subject of 'يقول' or something else. The commentator argues it cannot be from 'يقول' in the standard version.
2
Understand the two textual versions
The standard version read before the author contains the phrase 'وبعد فان العبد' which creates three preventers. The old version has 'مجليا ومصليا ليقول العبد المتوسل إلى الله' which is free of these.
Textual criticism is part of usul al-fiqh to ensure the correct basis for legal reasoning.
3
Analyze the three preventers
List and explain each: (1) The واو is a conjunction; a part of the conjoined item cannot precede the conjunction. (2) The particle إن requires beginning of speech; nothing after it can govern what precedes. (3) The implied annexed noun 'الحمد والصلوة' would cause useless repetition.
4
Apply the reasoning to the old version
In the old version, all three preventers are absent (no واو before 'يقول', no إن, no بعد with an implied noun), so 'حامدا' can be a حال from 'يقول'.
5
Recognize the practical impact
The choice of grammatical parsing affects the flow of meaning. In the standard version, 'حامدا' must be a حال from an earlier implied subject (the basmala), not from 'يقول'. This changes how the author's opening is understood.
In usul, such details can influence the legal inference drawn from the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجوز ان يكون حامدا حالا من فاعل يقول لان قوله وبعد فان العبد على مافي النسخة المقروة عند المصنف صارف عن ذلك واما على النسخة القديمة الخالية عن هذا الصارف فالظاهر انه حال عنه. ترجمہ! اور جائز نہیں ہے کہ حامداً یقول کے فاعل سے حال بنے کیونکہ مصنف کا قول وبعد فان العبد جیسا کہ نسخہ مقروة عند المصنف میں ہے اس سے مانع ہے اور لیکن نسخہ قدیمہ کے مطابق جو کہ اس مانع سے خالی ہے پس راجح یہ ہے کہ حامداً اس یقول سے حال ہے۔ جواب سوال مقدر۔ سوال ! ہوتا ہے کہ حامداً کو ابتدا کی ضمیر سے حال بنانے کی بجائے یقول کی ضمیر سے حال بنانا اولی وانسب ہے کیونکہ وہ جزء کتاب ہے جبکہ تسمیہ کا جزء ہونا مشکوک مشتمل ہے اس سے حال کیوں نہیں بنایا گیا۔ جواب انسخہ مقروہ وموجودہ کے مطابق یقول سے حال بنانا صحیح نہیں ہے اور عدم صحت کی تین وجوہ ہیں ۔ وجہ (۱) وبعد فان العبد میں واؤ حرف عطف ہے ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ معطوف کے اجزاء میں سے کوئی جزء حرف عطف پر مقدم نہیں ہوسکتا کیونکہ اس صورت میں حرف عطف کا بین اجزاء المعطوف واقع ہونا لازم آئے گا جو کہ ناجائز ہے مثلا ضربت زیر آوا کرمت عمروا میں ضربت زید عمر وا وا کر مت کہنا درست نہیں ہے اگر حامد کو یقول سے حال بنایا جائے تو یہ معطوف کا جزء ہوگا لہذا اس کی تقدیم علی حرف الواو العاطفہ جائز نہ ہوگی حالانکہ یہاں مقدم ہے۔ وجہ (۲) یہ ہے کہ فان العبد میں ان موجود ہے جو مقتضی صدارت کلام ہے اور اس کے مابعد اجزاء میں سے کوئی جزء ماقبل میں عامل نہیں ہوسکتا ورنہ صدارت فوت ہو جائیگی لہذا لیقول حامدا میں عمل نہیں کر سکتا۔ وجہ (۳) یہ ہے کہ بعد کا مضاف الیہ محذوف منوی ہے وہ الحمد والصلوۃ ہے تو عبارت اس طرح بنے گی و بعد الحمد والصلوة يقول العبد حامد اللہ تعالی اس میں تکرار بلا فائدہ ہے اگر نسخہ قدیمہ کو لوظ رکھا جائے جس کی عبارت اسطرح ہے مجلیا ومصلیا لیقول العبد المتوسل الی اللہ تو حامد اکو لقول سے حال بنانا درست بلکہ راج ہے کیونکہ اس عبارت میں موانع ثلاثہ مرتفع ہیں نہ واؤ ہے نہ ان ہے اور نہ بعد ہے
And it is not permissible that 'حامدا' be a حال from the subject of 'يقول' because the author's statement 'وبعد فان العبد' according to the copy read before the author prevents that. As for the old copy free from this preventer, the apparent is that it is a حال from it. Translation: And it is not permissible that 'حامدا' be a حال from the subject of 'يقول' because the author's statement 'وبعد فان العبد' as in the copy read before the author prevents that. And as for the old copy which is free from this preventer, the preponderant is that 'حامدا' is a حال from 'يقول'. Answer to an implied question: The question arises: why was 'حامدا' not made a حال from the subject of 'يقول' instead of from the implied subject of the basmala, since 'يقول' is a part of the book while the basmala's being part is doubtful? Answer: According to the read and existing copies, making it a حال from 'يقول' is not correct, and there are three reasons for its incorrectness: Reason (1): In 'وبعد فان العبد', the واو is a conjunction. The rule is that no part of the conjoined item can precede the conjunction, because then the conjunction would necessarily fall between parts of the conjoined, which is impermissible. E.g., in 'ضربت زيدا وعمرا', you cannot say 'ضربت وعمرا زيدا'. If 'حامدا' is made a حال from 'يقول', it would be part of the conjoined item, so its precedence over the conjunction would not be permissible, whereas here it is preceded. Reason (2): In 'فان العبد', there is 'إن' which necessitates being at the beginning of speech, and no part after it can be an operator on what precedes, otherwise the beginning status is lost. So 'يقول' cannot operate on 'حامدا'. Reason (3): The noun of 'بعد' is omitted but intended, it is 'الحمد والصلوة', so the expression would be 'وبعد الحمد والصلوة يقول العبد حامدا الله تعالى', and this contains useless repetition. If the old copy is adopted, whose expression is 'مجليا ومصليا ليقول العبد المتوسل إلى الله', then making 'حامدا' a حال from 'يقول' is correct, rather preponderant, because in this expression the three preventers are removed: there is no واو, no إن, and no بعد.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the author's opening sentence, specifically the grammatical status of the word 'حامدا'. The commentator first states the general ruling: it is not permissible to take 'حامدا' as a حال from the subject of 'يقول' according to the version of the text read before the author. However, in an older version, it is allowed. The commentator then presents an objection: why not make 'حامدا' a حال from 'يقول' since 'يقول' is definitely part of the book, whereas the basmala's status is uncertain? The response provides three reasons that prevent this interpretation in the standard version: (1) The واو in 'وبعد' is a conjunction, and a part of the conjoined item cannot precede the conjunction; (2) The particle 'إن' requires that nothing after it acts upon something before it; (3) The implied annexed noun ('الحمد والصلوة') would cause redundancy. In the older version without these issues, the analysis changes. This illustrates the importance of textual variants and grammatical analysis in usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
حال (haal): A circumstantial accusative that describes the state of the subject or object at the time of the action.
معطوف (ma'tuf): The conjoined item in a conjunction phrase.
صدارت (sadaarat): The property of a particle (like إن) to be at the beginning of a sentence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is one reason why 'حامدا' cannot be a حال from the subject of 'يقول' in the standard version?
A) Because 'يقول' is not a part of the book.
B) Because the واو in 'وبعد' is a conjunction and a part of the conjoined item cannot precede it.
C) Because 'حامدا' is a proper noun.
D) Because the old version prohibits it.

Key Takeaway
The grammatical function of 'حامدا' depends on the textual version; the standard version blocks it as a حال from 'يقول' due to three Arabic syntax rules.

The Extended Beginning: Resolving the Haal Contemporaneity Issue
Analyzing grammatical haal in book openings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the grammatical role of circumstantial accusatives in introductory phrases and apply the Hanafi principle of customary extension to resolve apparent temporal incongruity.

Core Idea
A book's beginning is a customary extended period, enabling the praising action to be contemporaneous with it.

This passage delves into a nuanced grammatical issue in the opening of classical Hanafi texts: how can the words 'haamidan' (praising) and 'musalliyan' (sending blessings) be proper circumstantial accusatives for the act of beginning, given that the praising occurs after the initial basmalah? The commentator Misk al-Maleeh provides a sophisticated answer by reinterpreting 'ibtida' as a customary extended period, not an instantaneous moment. This resolution demonstrates the interplay between Arabic grammar and legal methodology in Hanafi scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Grammatical Problem
Recognize the apparent contradiction: the circumstantial accusative (haal) must be contemporaneous with its operative word ('ibtida'), but the praising action ('haamidan') occurs after the initial utterance of basmalah.
The objection is that haal must coincide in time with the operative word.
2
Analyze the Redefinition of 'Ibtida'
Understand that the commentator defines 'ibtida' as a customary extended period from the start of composition to the beginning of research, not a single moment. This allows the praising and blessings (which occur within that period) to be contemporaneous.
The key term 'ibtida' is interpreted broadly to maintain grammatical coherence.
3
Examine the Second Objection and Its Resolution
A further objection tackles the second 'haamidan' (referring to praise in the Hereafter). The resolution reinterprets it as intention and determination, which occur at the time of beginning.
The resolution avoids temporal incongruity by shifting from literal occurrence to mental intent.
4
Evaluate the Charge of Combining Literal and Figurative
The commentator addresses the accusation that this interpretation combines haqiqah (literal) and majaz (figurative) in one word, which is disallowed. He posits an implicit 'haamidan' before 'thaniyan' to avoid the issue.
This demonstrates the Hanafi care for usul principles even in grammatical analysis.

فان قلت من شرط الحال المقارنة للعامل والاحوال المذكورة اعنى حامد أو غيره لا تقارن الابتداء بالتسميه قلت ليس الباء صلة لا بتدئ بل الظرف حال والمعنى متبركاً باسم الله ابتدأ الكتاب والا بتداء امر عرفي يعتبر ممتد امن حين الاخذ فى التصنيف الى الشروع في البحث ويقارنه التبرك بالتسمية والحمد والصلوة.
ترجمہ! پس اگر تو کہے کہ حال کی شرط سے ہے مقارنت عامل کے لئے اور احوال مذکورہ مراد رکھتا ہوں میں حامد أو غیرہ نہیں ہیں مقارن ابتداء بالتسمیہ کے ساتھ ۔ میں کہتا ہوں کہ نہیں ہے باء ابتداء کا صلہ بلکہ ظرف حال ہے اور معنی یہ ہے قبر کا باسم اللہ ابتداء الکتاب اور ابتداء ایک امر عرفی ہے اعتبار کی جائیگی لمبی تصنیف میں شروح ہونے کے وقت سے لیکر بحث میں شروع ہونے تک اور مقارن ہو گا اس ابتداء کو برکت حاصل کرنا تسمیہ اور حمد اور صلوٰۃ کے ساتھ ۔

غرض جواب وسوال ۔ سوال! ہوتا ہے کہ حامداومصلیا وغیرہ کو ابتدا سے حال بنانا درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ حال اور ذ والحال کے عامل کا زمانہ واحد ہوتا ہے یہاں ایسا نہیں ہے کیونکہ ابتداء بالتسمیہ کا زمانہ پہلے ہے اور حمد و صلوۃ کے صدور کا زمانہ بعد میں اگر چہ تاخیر قلیل ہو ایک سیکنڈ یا لحظہ ۔ جواب! اعتراض مذکور کا مدار اس پر ہے کہ بسم اللہ کو ظرف لغو بنا کر ابتدا کا صلہ بنایا جائے حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہے بلکہ بسم اللہ جار مجرور متبرک کے متعلق ہو کر ابتدا سے حال ہے ( کما ذکرنا من قبل ) اسی طرح حامد او مصلیا بھی احوال ہیں اور ابتداء سے مراد ابتداء عرفی ہے اور ابتداء عرفی کا زمانہ ممتد ہوتا ہے من شروع الکتاب الى بحث المقاصد یہ سارا ابتداء کا زمانہ ہوگا اور اسی زمانہ میں حمد کا صدور وصلوٰۃ کا وقوع اور تبرک بالتسمیہ کا وقوع ہوگا۔ تو زمانہ ابتداء وزمانہ حمد وصلوۃ میں اتحاد ومقارنت ثابت ہوگئی اسلئے حال بنانا صحیح ہے۔

فان قلت فعلى الوجه الثالث يكون حامدا ثانيا بمعنى ناويا الحمد وعازماً عليه ليكون مقارناً للعامل وحينئذ يلزم الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز قلت يجعل من قبيل المحذوف اى و حامداً ثانيا بمعنى عازماً عليه فلا يلزم الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز.
ترجمہ! پس اگر تو کہے کہ پس وجہ ثالث کے مطابق ہوگا حامد ثانیا بمعنی ناویاً للحمد اور عاز ما علی الحمد (یعنی حمد کی نیت وعزم کرنے والا ) تا کہ ہو جائے مقارن عامل کیلئے اور اس وقت لازم آئے گا جمع بین الحقیقة والمجاز ۔ میں کہتا ہوں کہ اسکو محذوف کے قبیلہ سے بنایا جائیگا یعنی حامد الثانیاً بمعنی عازم علی الحمد پس جمع بین الحقیقت والمجاز لازم نہیں آئیگا۔

غرض جواب سوال لیکن یہ سوال و جواب ایک اور سوال پر موقوف ہے جس کو شارح نے ذکر نہیں فرمایا۔ سوال یہ ہوتا ہے کہ سابق میں آپ نے مقارنت احوال مع زمانہ کا اصل فعل ابتداء کی جو صورت بیان فرمائی تھی کہ ابتد ا سے مراد امر عرفی محمند ہے الی مقاصد الکتاب اور حد وصلوٰۃ بھی اسی زمانہ میں واقع ہور ہے ہیں تو اسطرح مقارنت مع العامل متحقق ہو جائے گی یہ توجیہ حامد ا اولا میں تو مفید و کارگر ہو سکتی ہے لیکن وانیا میں مفید نہیں ہو سکتی کیونکہ تو جیہ ثالث کے مطابق ثانیا سے حمد فی الآخرہ مراد ہے تو حمد کا وقوع تو زمان آخرت میں ہوگا لہذا حالانکہ ابتداء بالکتاب کا زمان دنیا میں ہے حال کی مقارنت عامل کیساتھ باعتبار زبان ناممکن ہے کیونکہ زمانہ دنیا و آخرت میں بون بعید ہے۔ جواب! اس سوال کا یہ دیا گیا ہے کہ دریں صورت جب حمد کی نسبت اولا کی طرف ہوگی تو اس کا حقیقی معنی مراد ہوگا اور جب ثانیا کی طرف ہوگی تو مجازی معنی نیست حمد و عزم علی احمد مراد ہوگا مقصد یہ ہو گا جب میں اس کتاب کا آغاز کر رہا ہوں تو میں آخرت والی حمد کی نیت کرنے والا اور اس پر عزم کرنے والا ہوں تو نیت و عزم کا زمانہ ابتداء کتاب کے زمانہ کے ساتھ متحد ہے کیونکہ ابتداء کتاب کے زمانہ کے وقت ہی اس کا ارادہ و عزم محمد فی الآخرہ ہے تو مقارنت ثابت ہو جائے گی پھر اس اشکال کے جواب پر اشکال ہو اشارح تفتازانی اس کو ذکر کر کے جواب دے رہے ہیں ۔ اشکال! یہ ہے کہ اس جواب کی صورت میں جمع بین الحقیقۃ والمجاز لازم آتا ہے کیونکہ جب لفظ حمد کی نسبت اولا کی طرف ہوگی تو حقیقی معنی مراد ہوگا جب ثانیا کی طرف ہوگی تو نادیا کے معنی میں ہو کر مجازی معنی مراد ہوگا فذالک باطل ۔ جواب! (1) شارح کے جواب کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ یہاں جمع بین الحقیقة والمجاز فی لفظ واحد لازم نہیں آ رہا ہے بلکہ ثانیا سے پہلے حامد ا مقدر ہے اس سے مجازی معنی ( نادیا ) مراد لیا جا رہا ہے عبارت اس طرح ہوگی حامد اللہ تعالی اولا و حامد ا ثانیا اول حامد اسے حقیقی خانی
Misk al-Maleeh: Commentary on al-Tawdih. He turns the reins of praise only towards Allah, so in 'inan al-thana' the mention is the necessary concomitant and the intention is the implicative, and such a metaphor and figurative usage cannot be intended as 'haamidan'. Thus the objection is repelled. And in it is an indication that the one entering into the Islamic sciences should turn away from the side of creation and turn the reins of praise from all directions towards the side of the Truth, Exalted and Sanctified, knowing that He alone is deserving of praise. Translation: And in it is an indication that for the beginner in Islamic sciences, it is appropriate to turn away from creation and turn the reins of praise from all directions towards the side of Allah, Exalted and Sanctified, in a state of being certain that He alone is deserving of praise. The author's phrase indicates that whoever begins Islamic sciences, it is appropriate for him to turn away from Allah's creation and turn towards Allah, and consider only Allah deserving of praise. Then if you say: From the condition of the circumstantial accusative (haal) is contemporaneity with the operative word, and the mentioned ahwaal, i.e. 'haamidan' or other, are not contemporaneous with the beginning with the basmalah. I say: The ba is not a connector for 'abtadi', rather the adverb is a circumstantial accusative, and the meaning is 'blessing myself with the name of Allah, I begin the book', and 'al-ibtida' is a customary matter considered extended from the time of starting the composition to the beginning of the research, and the blessing with the basmalah, hamdalah, and salawat are contemporaneous with it. Translation: So if you say: The condition for the circumstantial accusative is contemporaneity with the operative word, and the mentioned ahwaal, I mean 'haamidan' or others, are not contemporaneous with the beginning with the basmalah. I say: The ba is not a connector for 'abtadi', rather the adverb is a circumstantial accusative, and the meaning is 'blessing myself with the name of Allah, I begin the book', and 'al-ibtida' is a customary matter considered as extended from the time of starting the composition to the beginning of research, and the blessing with the basmalah, hamdalah, and salawat will be contemporaneous with it. In short, question and answer. Question: It is not correct to make 'haamidan' and 'musalliyan' etc. into a circumstantial accusative for 'ibtida' because the rule is that the time of the circumstantial accusative and its operative word must be one, and that is not the case here because the time of beginning with the basmalah is earlier and the time of producing hamd and salat is later, even if the delay is small, a second or an instant. Answer: The basis of the mentioned objection is that 'bismillah' is taken as a redundant adverb and made a connector for 'ibtida', whereas it is not so; rather 'bismillah' is a prepositional phrase related to 'mutabarrikan' and is a circumstantial accusative for 'ibtida' (as we mentioned before). Similarly, 'haamidan' and 'musalliyan' are also circumstances, and by 'ibtida' is meant the customary beginning, and the time of the customary beginning is extended from the start of the book to the discussion of the topics; this entire period is the time of beginning, and within this time the occurrence of hamd, salat, and the blessing with the basmalah occur. So unity and contemporaneity between the time of beginning and the time of hamd and salat is established, therefore making them circumstantial accusatives is correct. Then if you say: On the third interpretation, 'haamidan' becomes second meaning 'intending hamd and resolved upon it' to be contemporaneous with the operative word, and then combination of literal and figurative meaning becomes necessary. I say: It is made from the category of deletion, i.e. 'and haamidan' second meaning 'resolved upon it', so combination of literal and figurative does not occur. Translation: Then if you say: According to the third interpretation, 'haamidan' becomes second meaning 'intending hamd and resolved upon it' to be contemporaneous with the operative word, and then combination of literal and figurative meaning becomes necessary. I say: It is made from the category of deletion, i.e. 'and haamidan' second meaning 'resolved upon it', so combination of literal and figurative does not become necessary. In short, question and answer: However, this question and answer depend on another question which the commentator did not mention. The question is: Previously you presented the form of contemporaneity of circumstances with the time of the actual operative word 'ibtida' such that by 'ibtida' is meant a customary extended matter up to the topics of the book, and hamd and salat also occur within that time; thus contemporaneity with the operative word is realized. This explanation can be useful and effective for 'haamidan' first, but not for 'haamidan' second, because according to the third interpretation, 'thaniyan' refers to hamd in the Hereafter, so the occurrence of hamd will be in the time of the Hereafter, whereas the time of beginning the book is in this world; contemporaneity of the circumstance with the operative word in terms of time is impossible because the times of this world and the Hereafter are far apart. Answer: The answer given to this question is that in that case, when hamd is attributed to 'awwalan', its literal meaning is intended, and when attributed to 'thaniyan', a figurative meaning is intended: intent of hamd and determination upon hamd. The purpose is: when I am beginning this book, I am one who intends the hamd of the Hereafter and is determined upon it, so the time of intention and determination is unified with the time of the beginning of the book, because at the time of beginning the book, his intention and determination for hamd in the Hereafter exists, so contemporaneity is established. Then upon the answer to this objection, an objection arises: the commentator Taftazani mentions it and gives an answer. The objection is: In the form of this answer, combination of literal and figurative becomes necessary, because when the word 'hamd' is attributed to 'awwalan', its literal meaning is intended; when attributed to 'thaniyan', it is in the meaning of intent, so figurative meaning is intended; and that is invalid. Answer: (1) The summary of the commentator's answer is that combination of literal and figurative in one word is not necessary here; rather, before 'thaniyan', 'haamidan' is understood, and from that a figurative meaning (intent) is taken. The phrase will be like this: 'haamidan li-Allah ta'ala awwalan wa haamidan thaniyan'; the first 'haamidan' is literal...
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is a detailed grammatical and legal analysis of the opening phrases of a typical Islamic scholarly work. The commentator, Misk al-Maleeh, is explaining Al-Tawdih's text regarding the basmalah, hamdalah, and salawat. The core issue is whether the circumstantial accusatives (ahwaal) like 'haamidan' (praising) can be properly attached to the operative word 'abtadi' (I begin) given that the praising occurs after the initial utterance of basmalah. The commentator argues that the 'beginning' is not a single moment but an extended customary period from the start of composition to the main discussion. Therefore, the hamd and salat, which occur within that period, are contemporaneous. He also addresses a further objection regarding the second instance of 'haamidan' (referring to praise in the Hereafter), resolving it by interpreting it as an intention and determination, which occurs at the time of beginning. Finally, he counters the charge of combining literal and figurative meaning by positing an implicit 'haamidan' before 'thaniyan'. This linguistic precision is typical of Hanafi usul analysis, where every word of the matn is scrutinized for legal implications.

Key Terms
حال (haal): A circumstantial accusative describing the state of the doer at the time of the action.
ابتداء (ibtidaa): The beginning of the book, considered as a customary extended period from starting composition to beginning research.
حقيقة (haqiqah): Literal meaning of a word.
مجاز (majaz): Figurative meaning of a word.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, why is it correct to make 'haamidan' a circumstantial accusative for 'ibtida'?
A) Because 'haamidan' is a proper noun and cannot be a circumstantial accusative.
B) Because 'ibtida' is a customary extended period, not a single moment, so the praising can be contemporaneous.
C) Because the basmalah is always recited after the hamdalah.
D) Because the commentator ignores the rule of contemporaneity.

Key Takeaway
The beginning of a book in Hanafi tradition is a customary extended period, allowing subsequent actions like praising to be grammatically proper as circumstantial accusatives.

Reason for Omitting the Prophet's Name
Commentator explains why the author omitted the Prophet's name.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two reasons given by the commentator for omitting the Prophet's name and explain how the textual variant (nuskha maqru'a) affects the analysis.

Core Idea
Omitting the Prophet's name can be a sign of profound respect, not disrespect.

In many Hanafi usul texts, authors sometimes omit the explicit name of the Prophet (peace be upon him) when praising him. This may seem odd to a beginner, but the commentator reveals a deeper respect. In this lesson, we explore the reasoning behind this omission and the subtlety of the author's choice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the presumed question
The commentator begins by stating a question that might arise: why did the author not mention the Prophet's name explicitly, especially in a context of praise where naming the praised is customary?
This shows the commentator's awareness of potential objections.
2
Analyze the first answer: respect
The first answer is that the omission was out of respect and veneration. Calling a great personality by name can be seen as bad manners, similar to calling one's teacher or father by name.
The commentator uses the phrase 'ta'zeeman wa ijlaalan' (out of respect and veneration).
3
Analyze the second answer: unambiguous description
The second answer is that explicit mention is needed to remove ambiguity, but here the attribute 'afdal al-rusul' (best of messengers) uniquely identifies the Prophet. No one else can be described that way, so the mind cannot turn to anyone else.
This reasoning relies on the uniqueness of the Prophet's rank.
4
Consider the textual variant
The commentator notes that this omission is according to the recited copy (al-nuskha al-maqru'a) used by the author. In another version, the Prophet's name is explicitly mentioned, which would remove the objection entirely.
This shows the commentator's attention to manuscript variations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفی ترك التصريح باسم النبي عليه السلام على مافى النسخة المقرؤة تنويه بشانه و تنبيه على ان كونه افضل الرسل امر جلى لا يخفى على احد . ترجمہ! اور نبی کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم کے نام کی تصریح کے چھوڑ دینے میں نسخہ مقروہ عند المصنف کے مطابق آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی شان کو بلند کرنا ہے اور اس بات پر تنبیہ کرنا ہے کہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا افضل الرسل ہونا واضح امر ہے کسی پر مخفی نہیں ہے۔ جواب سوال مقدر۔ سوال ! ہوتا ہے کہ مصنف نے نبی کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم کا نام مبارک کیوں نہ ذکر کیا حالانکہ نام کا ذکر کرنا اولی والیق بالمقام تھا اس لیے کہ مقام مدح میں ممدوح کی تعیین اولی ہوتی ہے۔ جواب ! (۱) تنو یہ بشانہ سے شارح جواب اول ذکر فرما رہے ہیں کہ تعظیماً واجلالاً نام کوترک کردیا کیونکہ الوالعظم وصاحب المرتبت شخصیت کو نام کے ساتھ پکارنے میں سوء ادب ہے کا الاستاذ ولوالد - جواب ! (۲) مجروح کے نام کی تصریح اس لیے کی جاتی ہے تاکہ مسمی تعیین ہو جائے ابہام نہ ہو یہاں ابہام نہیں ہے کیونکہ جو وصف افضل الرسل یہاں ذکر کی گئی ہے وہ نبی کریم ہی ہے کے علاوہ کسی اور میں متحقق ہی نہیں ہو سکتی ذہن کسی اور طرف متوجہ ہی نہیں ہو سکتا اسلئے نام کی تصریح کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ نوٹ ایر اشکال نسخہ مقروہ کو مقررہ عند المصنف پر ہے کہ بکہ اس میں اسم النبی میں نے نہیں ہے نسخہ غیر مقروہ میں تصریح باسم النبی اللہ ہے فلا اشکال علیھا ۔ اسم
And in leaving out the explicit mention of the name of the Prophet, peace be upon him, according to the recited copy (at the author), there is an elevation of his status and a reminder that his being the best of messengers is an obvious matter not hidden from anyone. Translation: In leaving out the explicit mention of the name of the Prophet, peace be upon him, according to the recited copy in the author's view, it is to elevate his status and to alert that his being the best of messengers is a clear matter, not hidden from anyone. Answer to a presumed question: A question arises: Why did the author not mention the blessed name of the Prophet, peace be upon him, while mentioning the name would have been more appropriate and suitable to the context, because in a context of praise, specifying the praised one is more appropriate? Answer (1): From 'tanawwuh bi shānihi' the commentator gives the first answer that out of respect and veneration he left out the name, because calling a great and high-ranking personality by name is bad manners, like [calling] a teacher or father. Answer (2): Explicit mention of a praised person's name is done so that the named one is determined and there is no ambiguity. Here there is no ambiguity, because the attribute 'best of messengers' mentioned here applies only to the Prophet and cannot be realized in anyone else; the mind cannot turn to anyone else. Therefore, there is no need for explicit mention. Note: There is an objection to the recited copy being the established one with the author because it does not contain the name of the Prophet. In the non-recited copy, there is explicit mention of the name of the Prophet, so there is no objection against it. The name.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of why the author (of the matn) omitted the explicit name of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in the introduction. The commentator (sharih) explains that this omission is actually a form of respect (tanzih) and a subtle reminder that the Prophet's status as the best of messengers is so obvious that no explicit naming is needed. The commentator then answers a presumed objection by providing five reasons: (1) Respect: calling a great person by name could be disrespectful, like addressing a teacher or parent by name. (2) No ambiguity: the attribute 'afdal al-rusul' uniquely identifies the Prophet. (3) The recited version (al-nuskha al-maqru'a) omits the name, while another version includes it, so there is no problem. The note clarifies the version discrepancy, showing the commentator's awareness of textual variants.

Key Terms
تصریح (tasrih): Explicit mention or naming, especially of the Prophet's name.
نسخہ مقروہ (nuskha maqru'a): The recited copy or version of the text that the author used as the basis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the Prophet's name is too holy to be written.
D) Because the manuscript did not have space for the name.

Key Takeaway
Omitting the Prophet's name in a text can be an intentional act of respect and can be justified by the uniqueness of his attributes.

Lexical and Metaphorical Meanings in Usul: Talaba, Mujalla, Musalla
Commentator explains literal and figurative meanings of horse-racing terms

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the literal and metaphorical meanings of 'talaba', 'mujalla', and 'musalla' from the Hanafi textual tradition and explain how metonymy (tasmīyat al-maḥall bi ism al-ḥāl) operates in usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Literal meanings anchor usul; metaphorical extensions expand the law — knowing the distinction is key to correct istinbat.

This passage introduces key terms from the context of horse racing — talaba (horses gathered for a race), mujalla (the leading horse), and musalla (the follower). The commentator explains their literal and figurative uses, demonstrating a common usul tool: metonymy. Understanding such lexical shifts is crucial for correctly interpreting legal texts that employ metaphor.

Guided Path
1
Identify literal meanings
Read the passage and note the literal meanings: talaba = horses gathered for a race; mujalla = leading horse that wins; musalla = horse that follows the leader.
Literal meanings are the primary, physical referents.
2
Identify metaphorical meanings
The passage states that 'talaba' is used metaphorically for the racecourse itself (a metonymy: place named after its occupants). Also, 'mujalla' and 'musalla' are used to refer to the Prophet and his family in the context of salawat.
Metaphorical extension is a key tool in legal language.
3
Analyze the type of figurative transfer
Recognize 'tasmīyat al-maḥall bi ism al-ḥāl' (calling the place by the name of what resides in it) for talaba. For mujalla and musalla, there is a metaphorical analogy: the Prophet is the leader, his family the followers.
This is a specific form of majaz used in Hanafi usul.
4
Apply to usul: implications for legal interpretation
Understand that if a legal text uses such terms, one must determine whether the literal or metaphorical meaning is intended. This affects rulings.
For example, if a hadith says 'the mujalla is blessed', it may refer to the Prophet metaphorically.
5
Practice identifying metonymy in other usul contexts
Consider other examples: 'yad' (hand) can mean literal hand or power; 'ra's' (head) can mean leader.
Metonymy is a recurring feature in legal texts.

والحلبة بالسكون خيل تجمع للسباق من كل اوب استعير للمضمار. ترجمہ! اور طلبہ (لام کے سکون کیسا تھ ) وہ گھوڑے ہیں جو جمع کئے جاتے ہیں ہر طرف سے گھوڑ دوڑ کے لئے مجاز بنایا گیا ہے میدان گھوڑ دوڑ کے لئے ۔ طلبہ کا لغوی و مجازی معنی بیان کر رہے ہیں حقیقی معنی وہ گھوڑے جو مختلف جوانب سے گھڑ دوڑ کیلئے جمع کیے جائیں۔ مجازی معنی میدان گھوڑ دوڑ من قبیل تسمیۃ المحل باسم الحال۔ والمجلى هو السابق من افراس السباق و المصلى هو الذى يتلوه لان راسه عند صلويه. ترجمہ! اور حیلی وہ گھوڑا ہے جو سبقت کرنے والا ہے دوڑ کے گھوڑوں سے اور مصلی وہ ہے جو اس کے پیچھے ہوتا ہے کیونکہ اسکاسر اس سابق کی سرین کے پاس ہوتا ہے۔ والتلو
And 'al-hilba' (with sukun) are horses gathered for a race from every direction; it is metaphorically used for the racecourse. Translation: And 'talaba' (with lam sukun) are horses that are gathered from every side for horse racing; it is used figuratively for the racecourse. They are explaining the literal and figurative meaning of 'talaba': the literal meaning is horses gathered from various directions for racing; the figurative meaning is the racecourse, by way of calling the place by the name of what resides in it. And 'al-mujalla' is the leading horse among the racehorses, and 'al-musalla' is the one that follows it, because its head is near its haunches. Translation: And 'mujalla' is the horse that outruns the other racehorses, and 'musalla' is the one that comes after it, because its head is near the haunches of the leading horse. And 'al-talu' [the following?].
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage provides lexical and metaphorical definitions for terms used in the author's introduction. The commentator starts by defining 'al-hilba' (or 'talaba' as per the context) as horses collected for racing, and then states that it is used metaphorically to mean the racecourse itself (a type of metonymy where the place is named after its occupants). Then he defines 'mujalla' as the leading horse (the winner) and 'musalla' as the second horse that follows, with its head at the haunches of the leader. This sets the stage for the metaphorical interpretation of these terms in relation to salawat (blessings) upon the Prophet and his family.

Key Terms
مجلی (mujalla): The leading horse in a race, the winner; metaphorically, the Prophet.
مصلی (musalla): The second horse that follows the leader; metaphorically, the family of the Prophet.
حلبہ (halaba): Literally, horses gathered for a race; metaphorically, the racecourse.
تسمیۃ المحل باسم الحال (tasmīyat al-maḥall bi ism al-ḥāl): A type of metonymy where the place is named after its inhabitants or what resides there.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Literal and metaphorical distinctions are essential in usul; the passage demonstrates metonymy and analogy as tools for understanding legal terms beyond their plain meanings.

Resolving Apparent Contradiction through Metaphorical Interpretation
Commentator resolves apparent contradiction via metaphorical expansion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five metaphorical interpretations the commentator offers to reconcile 'mujalla' and 'musalla', and apply the principle of ta'wil to similar textual tensions in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Being both the leading and following horse is not literal but metaphorical; ta'wil resolves apparent contradictions in scholarly discourse.

In this passage, the commentator anticipates a logical objection: how can the author claim to be both the foremost horse (mujalla) and the follower (musalla) in the field of salawat, when these are opposites? The commentator does not dismiss the objection but instead offers five distinct ta'wil (metaphorical interpretations) to show that the terms are meant figuratively. This lesson unpacks each resolution, revealing a key method of textual analysis in the Hanafi tradition—resolving literal tensions through context, hierarchy, and intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Apparent Contradiction
Recognize that the author's simultaneous claim to be both 'mujalla' (leading horse) and 'musalla' (following horse) appears to violate the logical principle that opposites cannot be combined (ijtimā' al-dhiddayn).
This sets up the need for metaphorical interpretation.
2
Understand the Objection
State the objection clearly: 'If the author is mujalla, he cannot also be musalla; the claim is false unless the terms are understood non-literally.'
The objection is presented as a presumed question.
3
List the Five Metaphorical Resolutions
Go through each of the five answers given by the commentator. They are: (1) multiplication/repetition, (2) primary vs. secondary reference, (3) different times, (4) beginning vs. end of the book, (5) different books.
Each resolution shows a different way to remove the literal contradiction.
4
Analyze Each Resolution
For each answer, explain the metaphorical mapping: what 'mujalla' and 'musalla' represent in that interpretation and why that resolves the tension.
Consider how the commentator uses context and purpose to shift from literal to figurative.
5
Extract the Broader Principle
Conclude that in Hanafi textual analysis, when a literal reading leads to impossibility or contradiction, ta'wil (metaphorical interpretation) is applied to find a coherent meaning. This principle is widely used in interpreting the Qur'an, hadith, and legal texts.
This is a key usul al-fiqh tool – not just for this passage, but for resolving apparent conflicts in primary sources.

Source Text

(۱) و معنی ذالک سے دے رہے ہیں کہ یہاں حقیقی معنی مراد نہیں مجازی معنی مراد ہے یعنی تکثر الصلوۃ اى مرة بعد مرة ۔ جواب ! (۲) محلی سے صلوۃ علی النبی اور مصلی سے صلوۃ علی اللآل مراد ہے کیونکہ صلوۃ علی النبی قصد او اصالت اور صلوۃ علی الآل تبعا و بالعرض ہے۔ جواب ! (۳) محلی و مصلی باعتبار از منہ مختلفہ مراد ہیں نہ کہ فی زمان واحد یعنی کسی وقت اول نمبر اور کسی وقت دوم نمبر ۔ جواب ! (۴) محلی سے ابتداء کتاب اور مصلی سے انتہاء کتاب مراد ہے عملا بالحدیث کہ ہر کام کی ابتداء و انتہاء میں اگر صلوۃ ہو تو وہ اقرب الی الا جابت ہو جاتا ہے۔ جواب ! (۵) مجلی سے کتاب اصحیح اور مصلی سے کتاب التوضیح مراد ہے۔
And the meaning of that is the multiplication and repetition of 'salah', or he indicated by 'mujalla' the sending of blessings upon the Prophet, peace be upon him, and by 'musalla' the sending of blessings upon the family (al), because it is implicitly and dependently. Translation: And the purpose of mujalla and musalla is the multiplication and repetition of salawat, or the author indicated by mujalla the salawat upon the Prophet and by musalla the salawat upon the family, because the latter is implied and subsidiary. Answer to a presumed question: The question arises: The author's statement 'I am mujalla and musalla in the field of salawat' is not correct; it would be a combination of opposites, for a horse is either mujalla or musalla, but cannot be both simultaneously; that would be a combination of opposites. Answer (1): From 'wa ma'na dhalika' they give that here the literal meaning is not intended, but the metaphorical meaning, i.e., the multiplication of salawat, meaning again and again. Answer (2): By mujalla is meant salawat upon the Prophet, and by musalla is meant salawat upon the family, because salawat upon the Prophet is primary and original, and salawat upon the family is secondary and incidental. Answer (3): Mujalla and musalla are meant with regard to different times, not at one single time, i.e., sometimes first rank and sometimes second rank. Answer (4): By mujalla is meant the beginning of the book, and by musalla the end of the book, acting upon the hadith that if salawat is sent at the beginning and end of every matter, it becomes closer to acceptance. Answer (5): By mujalla is meant the book al-Sahih, and by musalla the book al-Tawdih.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage addresses a potential objection: how can the author claim to be both the leading horse (mujalla) and the follower (musalla) in the field of salawat, when these are opposites? The commentator gives five metaphorical interpretations to resolve this: (1) The terms mean the multiplication and repetition of salawat (sending blessings again and again). (2) Mujalla refers to blessings upon the Prophet himself, while musalla refers to blessings upon his family, the latter being secondary. (3) They refer to different times (sometimes leading, sometimes following). (4) Mujalla refers to the beginning of the book, musalla to the end. (5) Mujalla refers to the Sahih book (perhaps Sahih Muslim?) and musalla to al-Tawdih (the matn being commented on). These answers show the commentator's deep engagement with rhetorical devices and his effort to reconcile apparent contradictions.

Key Terms
اجتماع ضدین (ijtimā' al-dhiddayn): Combination of opposites, considered impossible in logic; here raised as an objection to being both mujalla and musalla simultaneously.
صلوۃ علی الآل (salāt 'alā al-āl): Sending blessings upon the family of the Prophet, considered secondary to blessings upon the Prophet himself.
تأویل (ta'wīl): Metaphorical interpretation that shifts from the literal sense to a figurative meaning to resolve contradiction or harmonize texts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, which interpretation treats 'mujalla' and 'musalla' as referring to different books?
A) Answer (1): multiplication.
B) Answer (3): different times.
C) Answer (5): al-Sahih and al-Tawdih.
D) Answer (4): beginning and end of the book.

Key Takeaway
Apparent contradictions in scholarly or legal texts are often resolved through ta'wil (metaphorical interpretation), as demonstrated by the five responses in this passage—a core skill in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Rhetorical Devices in the Author’s Introduction: Tajnis and Beyond
Commentator explains rhetorical devices in the author's introductory sentences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the rhetorical device of tajnis (paronomasia) in Arabic texts and explain its function in the author’s introductory hamd and salawat sentences.

Core Idea
Tajnis uses similar-sounding words with different meanings to enrich textual expression — a key feature of classical Arabic prose.

The commentator highlights several rhetorical devices in the author’s opening phrases. Among them, tajnis stands out as a subtle play on words that deepens the text’s artistry. Understanding these devices is not mere ornamentation; it sharpens your sensitivity to the language of usul al-fiqh sources, where every word choice matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the devices mentioned
List the rhetorical terms the commentator points out in the hamd and salawat sentences: tajnis, isti'ara bil-kinayah, takhyil, tarshih, tamthil.
2
Define tajnis with the example
The commentator defines tajnis as two words identical in form but different in meaning, illustrating with 'thaniyan' in the text. Understand the two meanings: 'a second time' and 'one who turns back'.
3
Recognize the commentator's purpose
The commentator explains these devices to show the author's linguistic skill and to help the reader appreciate the text's beauty. In usul al-fiqh, rhetorical features can affect interpretation by clarifying ambiguity.
This is about textual appreciation, not ruling derivation.
4
Apply: Consider another example
Think of a common Arabic word that could be used in tajnis (e.g., 'ayn: eye/spring). While not in this text, recognizing such devices prevents misreading in legal contexts.

Source Text

ثم لا يخفى حسن ما في قرائن الحمد والصلوة من التجنيس وما في القرينة الثانية من الاستعارة بالكناية والتخييل والترشيح ومافي الرابعه من التمثيل . ترجمہ ! پھر نہیں ہے مخفی اس چیز کی خوبی جوحمد اور صلوٰۃ کے جملوں میں ذکر کی گئی ہے یعنی صنعت تجنیس اور جو چیز جملہ ثانیہ میں ذکر کی گئی ہے یعنی استعارہ بالکنایہ اور تخیلہ اور ترشیخیہ اور جو چیز ذکر کی گئی ہے جملہ رابعہ میں یعنی استعارہ تمثیلیہ ۔ غرض شارح ! حسن و خوبی عبارت متن و نکات بلاغت کا بیان ہے۔ فرانس قرینہ کی جمع ہے بمعنی مقرونہ یہاں سے جملہ مراد ہے کیونکہ جمل بھی ایک دوسرے سے ملے ہوتے ہیں قرائن کا لفظ ذکر کیا جمل نہ کہا کیونکہ یہ مستقل جملے نہیں ہیں۔ تجنیس ۔ پہلی خوبی یہ ہے کہ مصنف نے حمد و صلوۃ کے جملوں میں صنعت تجنیس کو استعمال کیا۔ صنعت تجنیس ، یہ ہے کہ دو لفظ ذکر کیے جائیں جو صورتا ایک جیسے ومجانس ہوں لیکن معنی مختلف ہوں جیسے جملہ کے فقرات میں ثانیا کو دومرتبہ ذکر کیا صورۃ تو مجانس ہیں لیکن معنی مختلف ہیں اول ثانیا کا معنی دوسری بار اور دوسرے ثانیا کا معنی پھیرنے والا اسی طرح جملہ صلوۃ
Then it is not hidden the beauty of what is in the sentences (qara'in) of praise (hamd) and salawat of tajnis (paronomasia), and what is in the second sentence of isti'ara bil-kinayah (metaphor by allusion), takhyil (imagination), tarshih (strengthening), and what is in the fourth of tamthil (allegory). Translation: Then the beauty of what is mentioned in the sentences of praise and salawat, namely the device of tajnis, and what is mentioned in the second sentence, namely isti'ara bil-kinayah, takhyil, tarshih, and what is mentioned in the fourth sentence, namely tamthil, is not hidden. In short, the commentator explains the beauty of the text's expression and rhetorical points. 'Fara'in' is the plural of 'qarinah' meaning conjoined; here it means sentence because sentences are also joined to one another. The word 'qara'in' is used, not 'jumal', because these are not independent sentences. Tajnis: The first beauty is that the author used the device of tajnis in the sentences of hamd and salawat. Tajnis is that two words are mentioned that are similar in form and homogeneous but differ in meaning, for example in the phrases of the sentence, 'thaniyan' is mentioned a second time; in form they are homogeneous but in meaning different: the first 'thaniyan' means 'a second time', and the second 'thaniyan' means 'one who turns back'. Similarly in the salawat sentence.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
In this concluding section, the commentator draws attention to the rhetorical beauties (muhasanat balaghiyya) in the author's introductory phrases of hamd (praise) and salawat (blessings). He identifies four sentences (qara'in) and the devices used in each: (1) tajnis (paronomasia) in the first sentence, (2) isti'ara bil-kinayah (metaphor by allusion), takhyil (imaginative depiction), and tarshih (reinforcement) in the second, (3) [third sentence not mentioned], (4) tamthil (allegorical simile) in the fourth. He then explains that 'qara'in' (plural of qarinah) is used instead of 'jumal' because these phrases are not fully independent sentences but are connected. He further describes tajnis: two words identical in script but different in meaning, giving the example of the word 'thaniyan' used twice in the text with different meanings (first: 'a second time', second: 'one who turns back'). This demonstrates the author's skill in rhetorical composition.

Key Terms
تجنیس (tajnis): A rhetorical device where two words are similar in form but have different meanings (paronomasia).
استعارہ بالکنایہ (isti'āra bil-kināya): A metaphor that alludes to something without directly naming it.
تمثیل (tamthīl): An allegorical comparison or simile.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Using words that rhyme.
B) Using two words that are similar in form but differ in meaning.
C) Using a metaphor that alludes to something.
D) Using an allegorical similitude.

Key Takeaway
The commentator highlights tajnis and other rhetorical devices in the author’s introduction to demonstrate the text’s literary artistry and to aid accurate reading.

Rhetorical Analysis of the Author's Introduction
Explaining the metaphorical meanings of mujalla and musalla and refuting objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the rhetorical devices (tajnis, isti'ara, tamthil, taqdim al-ma'mulat) used in the author's introduction and evaluate the commentator's responses to objections regarding contradictory terms and grammatical fronting.

Core Idea
The author's claim to be both mujalla and musalla is a rhetorical metaphor, not a literal contradiction.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih explains the metaphorical meanings of the terms 'mujalla' and 'musalla' used by the author in his introduction. The commentator not only clarifies that these terms are metaphorical, but also analyzes the rhetorical devices embedded in the text, including tajnis, isti'ara, and tamthil. Additionally, he addresses the objection regarding the fronting of objects in the phrases, providing reasons that align with the context.

Guided Path
1
Understand the literal meaning of mujalla and musalla
Recognize that in horse racing, mujalla is the first-place horse and musalla the second. This establishes the literal sense from which the metaphor is derived.
2
Identify the objection and the metaphorical reinterpretation
The objection is that one cannot be both first and second simultaneously. The commentator gives five metaphorical reinterpretations: (1) figurative meaning, (2) primary vs subordinate salat, (3) different times, (4) beginning vs end of book, (5) reference to two books.
These reinterpretations resolve the apparent contradiction.
3
Analyze the rhetorical devices highlighted by the commentator
Identify tajnis (paronomasia) in the praise and salat phrases, isti'ara bi al-kinnaya (metaphor by implication) with takhyil and tarshih in the second phrase, and isti'ara tamthiliyya (allegorical metaphor) in the fourth phrase.
Each device enhances the literary quality.
4
Examine the issue of taqdim al-ma'mulat
Understand the default rule (operator before operand) and the commentator's two reasons for fronting: (1) to maintain rhyme, (2) to show importance. Also understand why restriction (hasr) is not appropriate in this context.
Fronting here is stylistic, not indicative of restriction.

The good horse [mujalla] is the one that is first in the race, and musalla is the one that is second. The reason for naming musalla is that its head is next to the loins of the mujalla. And the meaning of that is the multiplication and repetition of the salat, or he indicated by al-mujalla the salat upon the Prophet, peace be upon him, and by al-musalla the salat upon the family, because it is implicitly and subordinately. [Then a response to a presumed objection:] The objection: The author's statement 'I am the mujalla and musalla in the field of salat' is incorrect because it is the combination of two opposites: a horse is either mujalla or musalla, it cannot be both simultaneously. Answer (1): The meaning is not literal but metaphorical, i.e., the multiplication of salat one after another. Answer (2): By mujalla is meant salat upon the Prophet, and by musalla is meant salat upon the family, because salat upon the Prophet is primary and original, while salat upon the family is subordinate and incidental. Answer (3): Mujalla and musalla are meant with respect to different times, not simultaneously – sometimes first, sometimes second. Answer (4): By mujalla is meant the beginning of the book, and by musalla is meant the end of the book, acting upon the hadith that every matter beginning and ending with salat is nearer to acceptance. Answer (5): By mujalla is meant the book al-Sahih [?] and by musalla is meant the book al-Tawdih. Then the beauty of what is in the phrases of praise and salat of tajnis, and what is in the second phrase of isti'ara bi al-kinnaya, takhyil, and tarshih, and what is in the fourth of tamthil, is not hidden. In summary, the commentator explains the beauty of the text's wording and rhetorical points. [Detailed explanation of tajnis, isti'ara, tamthil.] And the fronting of the objects in the last three phrases is for the sake of rhyme and emphasis, because restriction (hasr) is not appropriate for the context. [Response to another presumed objection:] Objection: The rule is that the operator precedes and the operand is delayed; the author fronted the objects 'in the handle of praise upon the most excellent of messengers' and 'in the arena of salat', acting against the principle. Answer: The author fronted them for two reasons: (1) to maintain rhyme – delaying them would break the rhyme; (2) these objects were more important than the operators, because the mention of Allah is important, and similarly 'upon the most excellent of messengers' is a statement of the excellence of the Messenger which is important. As for restriction, it is not appropriate for the context. [Further rebuttal:] Objection: You gave two reasons for fronting, but a third could be restriction, because the principle is 'fronting what should be delayed indicates restriction'. Answer: The commentator says the third reason (restriction) is not appropriate here for several reasons, one being that in the case of restriction the meanings would become wrong: the phrase 'and the reins of praise' would mean 'I only turn the reins of praise towards Allah, I do not praise others' – this restriction is false because praise of others is done, indeed it is sunnah; the hadith says 'He who does not thank people does not thank Allah'. So verbal thanks are given, praising the benefactor. And in 'upon the most excellent of messengers', if restricted, it would mean 'I only send salutations upon the most excellent of messengers and not upon any other messenger' – this is also incorrect because of the hadith...
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the author's introductory phrases, specifically the use of the terms 'mujalla' and 'musalla' (the first and second horse in a race). The commentator first explains the literal meaning: in horse racing, the mujalla is the first-place horse and the musalla is the second-place horse; the musalla's head is at the loins of the mujalla. Then he explains the metaphorical intention: the author does not mean literal horse-racing positions but rather the multiplication and repetition of salat upon the Prophet (ﷺ) and his family. The commentator gives five distinct answers to a presumed objection that the author cannot be both first and second simultaneously. The answers reinterpret the terms metaphorically: (1) the meaning is figurative, not literal; (2) mujalla refers to salat upon the Prophet (primary) and musalla to salat upon the family (subordinate); (3) the positions are at different times, not simultaneously; (4) mujalla refers to the beginning of the book and musalla to the end; (5) mujalla refers to the book al-Sahih and musalla to al-Tawdih. Then the commentator highlights the rhetorical beauties in the author's words: tajnis (paronomasia) in the praise and salat phrases, isti'ara bi al-kinnaya (metaphor by implication) with takhyil and tarshih in the second phrase, and isti'ara tamthiliyya (allegorical metaphor) in the fourth phrase. The commentator defines each rhetorical figure and shows how they apply. Finally, he addresses the issue of fronting objects (taqdim al-ma'mulat) in the last three phrases. The default rule is that the operator (factor) comes before the operand, but here the author fronted the objects. The commentator gives two reasons: maintaining rhyme (saj') and showing importance (ihtimam). He then refutes a possible objection that fronting implies restriction (hasr), because in this context restriction would lead to false meanings, such as restricting praise only to Allah or salutations only to the Prophet, which contradicts the sunnah of thanking and praising others.

Key Terms
المجلى (al-mujalla): In horse racing: the first-place horse. Metaphorically in the text: the primary salat upon the Prophet.
المصلى (al-musalla): In horse racing: the second-place horse. Metaphorically: the subordinate salat upon the family.
التجنيس (al-tajnis): A rhetorical device: using two similar-sounding words with different meanings.
الاستعارة بالكناية (al-isti'ara bi al-kinnaya): Metaphor by implication: a type of isti'ara where the metaphor is implied through a related attribute.
الاستعارة التمثيلية (al-isti'ara al-tamthiliyya): Allegorical metaphor: comparing a composite situation to another composite situation.
تقديم المعمولات (taqdim al-ma'mulat): Fronting the object or operand before its operator, contrary to the default order.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is one reason the author fronted the objects in the last three phrases?
A) To indicate restriction (hasr)
B) To maintain rhyme (saj')
C) To show the operator's importance
D) To follow the default grammatical rule

Key Takeaway
The commentator's rhetorical analysis shows that apparent contradictions in scholarly texts are often resolved by understanding metaphorical language and contextual concerns like rhyme and emphasis.

Rhetorical Analysis of Isti'ara in Legal Commentaries
Rhetorical analysis of the author's opening using balagha categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and classify types of isti'ara (metaphor) in a Hanafi usul text and explain their function in the author's argument.

Core Idea
Isti'ara makniyya and tamthiliyya are tools for comparing intangible concepts like praise and worship to tangible objects.

The author of this usul commentary opens with a series of rhetorical beauties. The first three involve wordplay and two kinds of metaphor: metonymic (makniyya) and representative (tamthiliyya). These metaphors enrich the text, making abstract actions vivid. In this lesson, you will dissect these rhetorical devices and understand how they shape the meaning of the author's opening.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two metaphors
Locate the passages where the commentator explicitly labels isti'ara makniyya and isti'ara tamthiliyya. Note what is being compared in each case.
The first compares praise (thana') to a fast horse; the second compares the collective efforts of worshippers to a horse race.
2
Classify the metaphors
Understand the difference: isti'ara makniyya attributes a property (speed) from the thing compared (horse) to the target (praise) without mentioning the horse explicitly. Isti'ara tamthiliyya likens a composite situation (worshippers striving) to another composite (horses racing).
The commentator explains that in the representative metaphor, a single form (hay'a) is abstracted from multiple elements.
3
Analyze the underlying comparisons
Identify the precise elements: praise is like a horse with a rein ('inan) indicating control; the worshippers' different ranks (sabiq, masbuq) correspond to first and second places in a race.
The metaphor implies that sending prayers upon the Prophet is a dynamic, competitive act.
4
Explain the rhetorical effect
Consider why the author used these metaphors: they make the abstract concrete, emphasize the honor of sending prayers, and engage the reader with vivid imagery.
In Hanafi usul, such rhetorical devices are part of the bayan (clarification) of the text's intended meaning.
