The Metaphor of Sealing and Opening: Analyzing Authorial Language in Usul Texts
Linguistic and rhetorical analysis of a preface metaphor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the rhetorical structure (tashbīh) in a classical usul preface and explain its function using the example of 'fadd al-khatm'.

Core Idea
A book before completion is like a sealed vessel; completion breaks the seal, granting access to its treasures.

This lesson examines the preface of Al-Tawdih, where the author uses a vivid metaphor: the incomplete book is a sealed object, hidden from view, and completion is like breaking the seal. The commentator dissects the Arabic terms 'fadd' and 'khitam' to clarify the metaphor. As usul students, understanding such rhetorical devices is crucial for appreciating the literary style of classical scholars and for correctly interpreting their intentions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the metaphor
Look for the comparative phrase 'بمنزلة' (like). Here, the book before completion is compared to a sealed thing.
The metaphor is explicit: 'جعل الكتاب قبل التمام ... بمنزلة الشئ المختوم'.
2
Break down the key terms
Define 'fadd' (breaking with separation) and 'khitam' (sealing clay) as the commentator does.
The commentator emphasizes that 'fadd' specifically means breaking with separation, not any break.
3
Examine the commentator's expansion
Note how the commentator elaborates on the two types of breaking (with/without separation) and specifies that 'fadd' is breaking with separation.
This precision is typical of usul commentators.
4
Understand the rhetorical purpose
The metaphor explains why the author withheld the book until completion and then presented it to students.
It highlights the transition from hiddenness to accessibility.
5
Apply to other texts
Recognize that similar metaphors appear in scholarly prefaces to convey humility or announce completion.
For example, authors often liken their work to a garden or a treasure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفض من فضضت ختم الكتاب اى فتحته والفض الكسر بالتفريق واختتمت الكتاب بلغت آخره والختام الطين الذي يختم به جعل الكتاب قبل التمام لاحتجابه عن نظر الانام بمنزلة الشئى المختوم الذي لا يطلع على مخزو ناته لا يحاط بمستو دعاته ثم جعل عرضه على الطالبين بعد الاختتام وعدم منعهم عن مطالعته بعد التمام بمنزلة فض الختام ترجمہ ! اور فض فضضت الكتاب سے ہے یعنی میں نے اسکو کھولا اور فض کا معنی ہے توڑنا جدا کرنے کیساتھ ۔ اور اختتمت الکتاب کا معنیٰ ہے میں اس کے آخر تک پہنچ گیا اور ختام کا معنی ہے وہ مٹی جس کے ساتھ مہر لگائی جائے یہ بنایا مصنف نے کتاب کو تمام ہونے سے پہلے اسکے پوشیدہ ہونے کی وجہ سے لوگوں کی نظر سے بمنزلہ شی مختوم کے (مہر لگائی ہوئی ) وہ جو کہ نہیں اطلاع حاصل کی جاسکتی اُس کے خزانوں پر اور نہیں احاطہ کیا جاسکتا اس کے مستودعات کے ساتھ (امانت رکھی ہوئی چیزیں) پھر بنایا اس کے پیش کرنے کو طلبہ پر اختتام کے بعد اور انکے نہ روکنے کو مطالعہ سے تمام ہونے کے بعد بمنزلہ ہر کو توڑنے کے۔ غرض فض ! کی تحقیق لغوی کا بیان فض کا لغوی معنی الکسر ( یعنی تو ڑنا ) پھر کسر کی دو صورتیں ہیں (۱) کسر با التفریق جس کا معنی ہے ریزہ ریزہ کرنا (۲) کسر بلا تفریق فض کا معنی الکسر با تفریق ہے اختتمت اختتام کا معنی بیان کیا بصورت محاورہ احتمت الكتاب ای بلغت آخرہ الختام سے ختام کا معنی بیان کیا وہ مٹی جس کے ساتھ مہر لگائی جاتی ہے۔ جعل الکتاب سے استعارہ بیان کر رہے ہیں مصنف نے کتاب توضیح کو قبل تمامہ تشبیہ دی ہے کئی مختوم کے ساتھ وجہ تشبیہ یہ ہے کہ شی مختوم کھولنے سے پہلے پوشیدہ ومستور عن نظر الا نام ہوتی ہے اس طرح کتاب قبل تمامہ مستور مجوب عن الناس تھی پھر بعد الانتقام طلبہ کے
And 'fadd' is from 'fadadtu khatma al-kitab' i.e. I opened it. Al-fadd means breaking with separation. 'Ikhtatamtu al-kitab' means I reached its end. Al-khitam is the clay with which it is sealed. He made the book before completion, because it was hidden from people's sight, like a sealed thing whose treasures and deposits cannot be accessed. Then he made presenting it to students after completion, and not preventing them from studying it after completion, like breaking the seal. ... Explanation: The linguistic meaning of fadd is breaking. There are two types of breaking: breaking with separation (into pieces) and breaking without separation. Fadd means breaking with separation. The meaning of 'ikhtatamtu' is given idiomatically: 'ikhtatamtu al-kitab' i.e. I reached its end. 'Al-khitam' is the clay used for sealing. The author (of the matn) uses a metaphor: the book before completion is like a sealed thing because it is hidden from view; after completion, presenting it to students is like breaking the seal.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage explains the author's metaphorical language in the preface of Al-Tawdih. The author says he 'opened the seal of the book' (fadadtu khatma al-kitab) after completing it. The commentator breaks down the terms: 'fadd' means breaking apart or opening by separating; 'ikhtitam' means reaching the end; 'khitam' is the sealing clay. The author compares the book before completion to a sealed object: its contents were hidden from people. After completion, however, he presents it to students, which is analogous to breaking the seal so that its hidden treasures become accessible. This is a common trope in classical Islamic scholarly writing, emphasizing that the completed work is now available for study. The commentator further clarifies that 'fadd' specifically implies breaking with separation (into fragments), not just any break, to emphasize the act of opening.

Key Terms
الفض (al-faḍḍ): الكسر بالتفريق (breaking with separation)
الختام (al-khitām): الطين الذي يختم به (the clay used for sealing)
اختتمت الكتاب (ikhtatamtu al-kitāb): بلغت آخره (I reached its end)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the author compare the book before completion to?
A) A sealed treasure
B) An unfinished building
C) A locked door
D) A blank page

Key Takeaway
The metaphor of sealing and opening in classical usul prefaces emphasizes that a completed work is now available for scholarly study, and its author has revealed its contents to the academic community.

Defending the Preposition: Critique of Taftazani's Objection on 'Lam Yasbiqni'
Critical refutation of a grammatical objection in Hanafi usul commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three justifications (tawjeehat) that refute Taftazani's objection regarding the preposition with 'sabaqa' and evaluate their validity in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Three linguistic justifications — Quranic usage, elevation nuance, and tadmin — render Taftazani's objection invalid.

This lesson examines a subtle linguistic critique by Taftazani against the author of al-Tawdih. The commentator provides three robust justifications to defend the preposition 'ila' with 'sabaqa'. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to engage with classical usul commentaries.

Guided Path
1
State Taftazani's objection
What exactly did Taftazani claim about the preposition? He argued that 'sabaqa' requires 'ala', not 'ila', so the author should have written 'lam yasbiqni ala mithlihi'.
The objection hinges on standard Arabic transitivity rules.
2
Examine the first justification: Quranic precedent
The commentator cites Quranic usage where 'sabaqa' takes 'ala' (e.g., 'wama nahnu bimusirrighina ala an nubaddila amthalakum'). This shows that 'ala' is permissible.
This is the strongest evidence because it comes from the Quran.
3
Examine the second justification: tasamuh and elevation
The author deliberately used 'ila' to imply 'uluww' (elevation), as if to say 'none has risen to my level'. This is a rhetorical license (tasamuh).
This justification appeals to the author's intentional stylistic choice.
4
Examine the third justification: tadmin
The verb 'sabaqa' is given the meaning of 'ghalaba' (overcome) or 'ittala'a' (become aware), which require 'ala'. This is a common Arabic device called tadmin (inclusion of meaning).
Tadmin is a well-known figure of speech in Arabic rhetoric.
5
Synthesize the refutation
The three justifications collectively prove that 'ala' is acceptable. The commentator concludes that Taftazani's objection is invalid, especially since Taftazani himself accused the author of excessive tasamuh elsewhere.
The refutation demonstrates the depth of linguistic analysis in usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ترتیب انیق ای حسن معجب يريد به بعض ما تصرف فيه من التقديم والتاخير في المباحث والا بواب على الوجه الاحسن الاليق والصواب لم يسبقنى الى مثله سبقت العالمين الى المعالي. ترجمہ یعنی خوبصورت تعجب میں ڈالنے والی ترتیب مصنف ارادہ کرتا ہے بعض ان تبدیلیوں کا جو اس کتاب میں کی ہیں یعنی تقدیم و تاخیر مباحث اور ابواب میں احسن والیق طریقے پر اور صواب یہ تھا کہ مصنف لم يسبقنی الی مثلہ کہتا ( بصلة الی ) ( جیسا کہ شاعر نے کہا ) سبقت العالمین الی المعالی ۔ غرض بیان معنی لغوی ! و توضیح متن ای حسن معجب سے انیق کا معنی لغوی بیان کیا بمعنی ایسا خوبصورت جو تعجب میں ڈال دے پھر وضاحت کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ اس ترتیب انیق سے مراد وہ تقدمات و تأخرات ہیں جو مصنف نے مباحث وابواب میں علی الوجہ الاحسن والا لیق اختیار فرمائے ہیں مثلا تقسیم ثانی کو ثالث اور ثالث کو ثانی بنانا وغيره، والصواب لم يسبقني الی مثله - غرض شارح! مصنف پر اشکال کر رہے ہیں کہ لم يسبقنی علی مثلہ کی بجائے الی مثلہ کہنا چاہئے تھا کیونکہ باب سبق متعدی بصلہ الی ہوتا ہے اس پر ایک شاعر عمر خیام کا شعر استشها را پیش کرتا ہے سبقت العالمين الى المعالی بصائب فكرة ب وعلو همته الخ تو یہاں بھی مصنف نے صلہ غلط ذکر کیا ہے۔ تبصرہ ! شراح و مشین رقم طراز ہیں کہ شارح کا یہ اشکال درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس نے والصواب کہا اور الصواب ضد الخطاء والغلط ہے اس کا اطلاق اس جگہ ہوتا ہے جہاں جانب مخالف کی کوئی توجیہ نہ ہو سکے حالانکہ یہاں متعدد تو جھات ہو سکتی ہیں۔ تو جیہ اول (۱) جس طرح سبق متعدی بصلہ الی ہوتا ہے اسی طرح بصلہ علی بھی متعدی ہوتا ہے۔ جیسا کہ قرآن پاک میں ہے و مانحن بمسیر قین علی ان نبدل امثالکم ۔ باقی استدلال ا تفتازانی من شعر الخیام پر بھی اشکال کیا گیا ہے کہ عمر خیام شعراء مولدین و متاخرین سے تعلق رکھتا ہے اور مولدین کے کلام سے استشھاد بالا جماع جائز نہیں ہے نیز وہ کبھی بھی ہیں اور کلام مجم سے بھی استشهاد جائز نہیں ہے۔ تو جیہ دوم (۲) مصنف نے تسامح اختیار کرتے ہوئے علی ذکر کیا اور اس تسامح غیر ارادی میں نکتہ یہ مضمر ہے کہ علی علو سے ہے مصنف نے اشارہ کیا کہ میں ایسی بلندی پر پہنچا ہوں کہ کوئی شخص وہاں تک نہ پہنچ سکا۔ توجہ ثالث (۳) مصنف نے صنعت تضمین ( واتضمین باب واسع في كلام العرب (وال نقل عن ابن جنی لو قلت تضمینات العرب لاجتمعت مجلدات) کو اختیار کیا سبق مضمن ہوگا معنی غلب یا اطلع یا وقف یا استعلاء کو پھر تضمین کی وہی دو صورتیں اختیار کی جائیں گی جو ند کورنی با قیل ہو چکی ہیں اول صورت میں عبارت ہوگی لم يسبقنی بمعنی کلم نسنی یا تم پیلینی علی مشکلہ اور ثانی صورت میں عبارت اس طرح ہوگی لم یسبقنی واقفا یا غالبای مستعلیا علی مثله وغیره خلاصه اینکه تین تو جیہات سے ثابت ہو گیا کہ سبق کا صلہ علی آ سکتا ہے تو شارح تفتازانی کا والصواب کہنا درست نہیں ہے حقیقت بات یہ ہے کہ شارح نے جب ایک مرتبہ کثیرا مالتسامح میں ذکر کر دیا ہے کہ مصنف بہت زیادہ تسامح کرتا ہے تو اس کے بعد بار بار تسامح والا اشکال کرنا لغو ہے۔
His statement: 'Elegant arrangement' i.e., beautiful and admirable. He intends by it some of the changes he made in the order of topics and chapters in the best and most fitting manner. And the correct thing is that the author should have said 'lam yasbiqni ila mithlihi' (with the preposition 'ila') as the poet said 'Sabaqtu al-alameena ila al-ma'ali'. The commentator objects that the author should have used 'ala' instead of 'ila' because the verb 'sabaqa' is transitive with 'ila'. Then three justifications are given: First, 'sabaqa' can also take 'ala' as in the Quran. Second, the author used 'tasamuh' (leniency) with a subtle point of 'uluww' (elevation). Third, the author used 'tadmin' (inclusion) where 'sabaqa' carries the meaning of 'ghalaba' or 'ittala'a'. Thus three justifications prove that 'ala' is acceptable. The commentator's objection is invalid.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a detailed linguistic dispute about the correct preposition with the verb 'sabaqa'. The author of Al-Tawdih wrote 'lam yasbiqni ila mithlihi' (none has preceded me to the like). Taftazani in his supercommentary objects that it should be 'ala' not 'ila'. The commentator of Miskulmaleeh refutes this with three arguments: (1) 'sabaqa' can take either prep., citing Quran; (2) the author intentionally used 'ila' to imply elevation; (3) the author employed 'tadmin' where the verb is given the meaning of 'ghalaba' or 'ittala'a', thus requiring 'ala' in the sense of 'over'. The refutation concludes that Taftazani's objection is baseless, especially since he himself previously accused the author of excessive leniency (tasamuh) and then nitpicks.

Key Terms
سبق (sabaqa): To precede; takes prepositions 'ila' or 'ala'.
تضمین (tadmin): Inclusion of meaning where a word carries the sense of another word, affecting its transitivity.
تسامح (tasamuh): Linguistic leniency or tolerance, where a word is used in a slightly extended sense.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT one of the justifications for the preposition 'ala' with 'sabaqa'?
A) Quranic usage
B) Tadmin (semantic inclusion)
C) Consensus of grammarians
D) Tasamuh to imply elevation

Key Takeaway
Linguistic objections in usul commentaries can be refuted by citing Quranic usage, rhetorical license, and semantic inclusion (tadmin).

Defending the Authorial Usage: Tadmeen and the Sabq Dispute
Defending author's use of 'على' with سبق against Taftazani's criticism

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the linguistic arguments (tadmeen, Quranic istishhad) used in Hanafi usul to defend the usage of 'sabaqa' with 'ala', and identify the methodological flaw in Taftazani's objection.

Core Idea
Tadmeen allows a verb to transfer transitivity, validating 'sabaqa bi-ala' through Quranic precedent.

In Hanafi usul, the soundness of a text's language is critical for deriving rulings. When Taftazani criticized the author's use of 'ala' with 'sabaqa', the commentator mounted a defense using three justifications. This lesson unpacks those arguments, focusing on tadmeen and the authority of Quranic usage, and reveals why Taftazani's objection fails.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested linguistic element
The verb 'sabaqa' is normally transitive with 'ila' (to precede towards). The author used 'ala' instead, claiming 'lam yasbiqni ila hadha al-amr' (he did not precede me in this matter). Taftazani objected to 'ala' as incorrect.
2
State Taftazani's objection and its basis
Taftazani claimed 'sabaqa' only takes 'ila', and the use of 'ala' is a grammatical error. He cited a line from Umar Khayyam's poetry as evidence for the correct usage.
Umar Khayyam is a later poet (mukhadramun), which is key to the critique.
3
Analyze justification 1: Quranic evidence
The commentator cites a Quranic verse (likely 17:101) where a verb of similar meaning (sara, qina, etc.) is used with 'ala', showing that such transitivity exists in the highest linguistic authority.
Quran: 'wa ma nahnu bi musirri qina ala an nubaddila amthalakum'
4
Analyze justification 2: Author's intentional meaning
The author used 'ala' deliberately to imply 'uluww' (height), indicating his elevated status. This is an intentional leniency (tasamuh) to convey a deeper meaning.
The preposition 'ala' shares the root with 'uluww'.
5
Analyze justification 3: Tadmeen
Tadmeen (inclusion) is a rhetorical device where a verb takes on the meaning of another verb, thereby adopting its transitivity. 'Sabaqa' is given the meaning of 'ghalaba' (overcome), 'ittala'a' (become aware), or 'ista'la' (rise), all of which govern 'ala'.
This is the most powerful justification, showing flexibility in Arabic.
6
Evaluate the refutation of Taftazani's citation
The commentator declares that citing later poets (mukhaddathun) is invalid by consensus (bilā jamā'). Taftazani's citation of Umar Khayyam is therefore baseless.
This highlights the hierarchy of linguistic authorities: Quran, then early Arab speech, then classical poets, but not later poets.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
توجیہ اول جس طرح سبق متعدی بصلہ الی ہوتا ہے اسی طرح بصلہ علی بھی متعدی ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ قرآن پاک میں ہے و مانحن بمسیر قین علی ان نبدل امثالکم۔ باقی استدلال ا تفتازانی من شعر الخیام پر بھی اشکال کیا گیا ہے کہ عمر خیام شعراء مولدین و متاخرین سے تعلق رکھتا ہے اور مولدین کے کلام سے استشھاد بالا جماع جائز نہیں ہے نیز وہ کبھی بھی ہیں اور کلام مجم سے بھی استشهاد جائز نہیں ہے۔ توجیہ دوم مصنف نے تسامح اختیار کرتے ہوئے علی ذکر کیا اور اس تسامح غیر ارادی میں نکتہ یہ مضمر ہے کہ علی علو سے ہے مصنف نے اشارہ کیا کہ میں ایسی بلندی پر پہنچا ہوں کہ کوئی شخص وہاں تک نہ پہنچ سکا۔ توجہ ثالث مصنف نے صنعت تضمین ( واتضمین باب واسع في كلام العرب وال نقل عن ابن جنی لو قلت تضمینات العرب لاجتمعت مجلدات) کو اختیار کیا سبق مضمن ہوگا معنی غلب یا اطلع یا وقف یا استعلاء کو پھر تضمین کی وہی دو صورتیں اختیار کی جائیں گی جو ند کورنی با قیل ہو چکی ہیں اول صورت میں عبارت ہوگی لم يسبقنی بمعنی کلم نسنی یا تم پیلینی علی مشکلہ اور ثانی صورت میں عبارت اس طرح ہوگی لم یسبقنی واقفا یا غالبای مستعلیا علی مثله وغیره خلاصه اینکه تین تو جیہات سے ثابت ہو گیا کہ سبق کا صلہ علی آ سکتا ہے تو شارح تفتازانی کا والصواب کہنا درست نہیں ہے حقیقت بات یہ ہے کہ شارح نے جب ایک مرتبہ کثیرا مالتسامح میں ذکر کر دیا ہے کہ مصنف بہت زیادہ تسامح کرتا ہے تو اس کے بعد بار بار تسامح والا اشکال کرنا لغو ہے۔
First justification: Just as sabq is transitive with 'ila', similarly it is transitive with 'ala'. As in the Quran: 'And we are not prevented from changing your likenesses.' The remaining objection to Taftazani's citation from Umar Khayyam's poetry is also criticized: that Umar Khayyam belongs to the later poets, and citing the speech of later poets is not permissible by consensus, nor is it permissible to cite ambiguous speech. Second justification: The author adopted leniency and mentioned 'ala', and in this unintentional leniency there is an implied point: that 'ala' is from 'uluww' (height). The author indicated that he reached such a height that no one else could reach. Third justification: The author adopted the device of tadmeen (inclusion). Sabq will include the meaning of ghalaba (overcoming), ittila' (becoming aware), wuqoof (stopping), or isti'la' (rising). Then the two forms of tadmeen previously mentioned are adopted. The first form: the phrase would be 'lam yasbiqni' meaning 'he did not precede me' or 'he did not overcome me in difficulty'. The second form: the phrase would be 'lam yasbiqni waqifan' or 'ghaliban' or 'musta'liyan'. In summary, three justifications prove that sabq can take 'ala' as a particle, so Taftazani's statement 'the correct view is...' is incorrect. The reality is that the commentator once said 'the author is very lenient', so repeatedly criticizing based on leniency is futile.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (ikhtilaf) between the commentator (likely Sadr al-Shariah) and Taftazani over the correct usage of the verb 'sabaqa' with the preposition 'ala'. The author of the matn (Sadr al-Shariah) wrote in his introduction: 'lam yasbiqni ila hadha al-amr' but Taftazani criticized it as incorrect because 'sabaqa' is transitive with 'ila', not 'ala'. The commentator defends the author with three justifications: First, 'sabaqa' can be transitive with 'ala' just as with 'ila', citing a Quranic verse (perhaps 17:101). Second, the author intentionally used 'ala' to indicate his high station, drawing from the root 'uluww' (height). Third, the author used the rhetorical device of tadmeen (inclusion), where 'sabaqa' takes on additional meanings such as 'ghalaba' (overcome) or 'ittala'a' (become aware), which do take 'ala'. The commentator also criticizes Taftazani's citation of Umar Khayyam's poetry, arguing that citing later poets is not valid. The conclusion is that the author's usage is correct, and Taftazani's repeated criticism based on leniency is baseless since he already acknowledged the author's leniency.

Key Terms
سبق (sabaqa): To precede, used here with 'ala' by inclusion (tadmeen) to mean overcome or become aware
تضمین (tadmeen): A rhetorical device where a word takes on the meaning of another word, thus changing its transitivity

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, how many justifications are provided to defend the use of 'ala' with 'sabaqa'?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defends the linguistic correctness of 'sabaqa bi-ala' through Quranic evidence, intentional connotation, and tadmeen, highlighting the importance of multiple argument layers in usul al-fiqh.

Parsing the Missing Connector in Usul Texts
Parsing the missing relative pronoun

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the missing relative pronoun in an adjectival clause and apply the Hanafi grammatical device of 'wad' al-zahir mawdi' al-mudmar' to resolve apparent grammatical gaps.

Core Idea
A missing pronoun in an adjectival clause is not a defect; it can be supplied by context or by the described noun itself.

In classical usul texts, grammatical precision is essential for correct legal interpretation. The phrase 'lam tablugh sifat tadqiqat' from the matn appears to lack a connector linking the adjectival clause to its antecedent. This lesson unpacks the commentator's two-part solution: either an omitted pronoun (al-aa'id al-mahzuf) or the device of placing the explicit noun in place of the implicit pronoun (wad' al-zahir mawdi' al-mudmar). Understanding this parsing is key to making sense of the author's claim about the unprecedented depth of investigation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the grammatical issue
Recognize that the clause 'lam tablugh sifat tadqiqat' is an adjective for the preceding noun. An adjectival clause requires a connector (aa'id) referring back to the described noun. Here, no explicit pronoun appears.
The question arises: where is the connector?
2
Examine the first solution: omitted pronoun
The commentator proposes that the pronoun 'ha' (her) is omitted but understood. The full phrase would be 'lam tablughaha farisan hadha al-ilm ila hadha al-ghayah'—'the knights of this science did not reach them to this end.'
In this reading, 'tadqiqat' is the antecedent, and the omitted 'ha' refers to it.
3
Examine the second solution: explicit noun as connector
Alternatively, the word 'tadqiqat' itself is repeated in the adjectival clause (or its equivalent 'tadqiq' appears). This is 'wad' al-zahir mawdi' al-mudmar'—placing the explicit in the place of the implicit. The phrase would be 'lam yablugh farisan hadha al-ilm ila hadha al-ghayah min al-tadqiq'.
Here, the described noun itself serves as the connector, making the clause self-contained.
4
Understand the transitivity of 'bulugh'
The verb 'bulugh' is normally transitive by itself, but here it is made transitive with 'ila'. This is justified by tadmeen—giving it the meaning of 'wusul' (arrival) which requires 'ila'.
This resolves the objection that 'ila' is grammatically unnecessary.
5
Apply to the original text
Now read the original phrase with awareness that both interpretations are valid. The choice depends on whether the 'ghayah' refers to a time limit or a degree of investigation.
This flexibility enriches the text's meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله لم تبلغ صفة تدقيقات والعائد محذوف اى لم يبلغها فرسان علم الاصول الى هذه الغاية من الزمان او المراد لم يصل فرسان هذا العلم الى تلك الغاية من التدقيق فيكون من وضع الظاهر موضع المضمر وتعدية البلوغ بالى لجعله بمعنى الوصول والانتهاء. غرض بیان ترکیب کر لم يبلغ فرسان هذا العلم إلى هذا الامد جمادیل کر تدقیقات کی صفت ہے۔ والعائد محذوف الخ ۔ غرض جواب سوال مقدر۔ سوال یہ ہوتا ہے کہ جب جملہ ماقبل کیلئے صفت واقع ہو تو اس میں کسی رابط کا ہونا ضروری ہے پھر رابطہ کی دو صورتیں ہیں (1) کبھی رابطہ ضمیر ہوگی (۲) کبھی موصوف بعینہ جملہ صنعتیہ میں مذکور ہوگا جو کہ رابطہ ہوگا یہاں رابطہ کی دو صورتوں میں سے کوئی بھی نہیں ہے۔ جواب شارح جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ مقام ہذا میں دونوں صورتیں ہو سکتی ہیں۔ اول صورت میں رابط ضمیر محذوف ہوگی عبارت ہوگی۔ لم يبلغها فرسان هذا العلم الى هذه الغالية ، اور اس غایت سے غایت زمانی مراد ہو گی مطلب ہوگا کہ اس زمانہ تک شہسوار علم اصول میں سے کوئی بھی ان تدقیقات تک نہیں پہنچ سکا۔ دوسری صورت میں الامد سے غایت تدقیقی مراد ہوگی تو گویا موصوف تدقیقات خود جملہ صنعتیہ میں مذکور ہوگا تو یہ من قبيل وضع المظهر موضع المضمر ہوگا جیسے الحاقہ ما الحاقہ کیونکہ مرجع کے مذکور ہونے کی وجہ سے موقع ضمیر کا تھا تو عبارت اس طرح ہوگی لم یبلغ فرسان هذ العلم الی هذه الغالبية من التدقیق تو موصوف تدقیق خود جملہ صفتیہ میں آگیا تو ربط حاصل ہو گیا۔ وتعدیۃ البلوغ جواب سوال بلوغ فعل متعدی بنفسہ ہوتا ہے اس کوالی کے ساتھ متعدی کرنا درست نہیں۔ جواب یہ دیا کہ صنعت تضمین کو اختیار کیا لم يبلغ بمعنی لم یصل اور لم ینتہ ہے۔
His statement: 'the description of careful investigations did not reach' – the relative pronoun is omitted, i.e., 'the knights of the science of usul did not reach them to this end of time.' Or it means: 'the knights of this science did not reach that end of investigation.' So it is placing the explicit noun in the position of the implicit pronoun. And making 'bulugh' transitive with 'ila' is to give it the meaning of 'wusul' (arrival) and 'intiha' (ending). The purpose is to explain the structure: 'lam yablugh farisan hadha al-ilm ila hadha al-amad' – making 'tadqiqat' an adjective. The relative pronoun is omitted, etc. So the answer to an implied question: The question is: when a clause is an adjective for the preceding clause, a connector is necessary. There are two types of connectors: sometimes a pronoun, sometimes the described noun itself mentioned in the adjectival clause. Here neither exists. The commentator answers that both types are possible. First type: the connector is a deleted pronoun; the phrase would be 'lam yablughaha farisan hadha al-ilm ila hadha al-ghayah', meaning no one has reached these investigations up to this time. Second type: the 'amad' refers to the ultimate investigation, so the described noun (tadqiqat) itself is mentioned in the adjectival clause, making it like 'al-haqu ma al-haq'? This is from placing the explicit in the position of the implicit, because due to the mention of the antecedent, a pronoun was appropriate. So the phrase would be 'lam yablugh farisan hadha al-ilm ila hadha al-ghayah min al-tadqiq'. So the described noun 'tadqiq' appears in the adjectival clause itself, achieving the connection. And regarding 'transitivity of bulugh': The question: 'bulugh' is inherently transitive; making it transitive with 'ila' is incorrect. The answer: the device of tadmeen is adopted, giving 'lam yablugh' the meaning of 'lam yasil' and 'lam yantahi'.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This is a grammatical parsing exercise (tarkib) of the phrase 'lam tablugh sifat tadqiqat' from the matn. The commentator explains that the phrase has an omitted relative pronoun (al-aa'id mahzuf). Two interpretations are possible: either the pronoun is deleted (first scenario) or the described noun itself serves as the connector (second scenario). A hypothetical objection is raised: since the clause is adjectival, a connector is required, but neither an explicit pronoun nor the described noun appears. The reply is that both are actually present in one of the two interpretations. In the first, the deleted pronoun is implied; in the second, the word 'tadqiq' (investigation) itself appears later in the clause, acting as a connector by substituting the pronoun. This is called 'placing the explicit in the position of the implicit' (wad' al-muzhir mawdi' al-mudmar). Additionally, the verb 'bulugh' is made transitive with 'ila' by giving it the meaning of 'wusul' (arrival) via tadmeen. Thus, the grammar is sound.

Key Terms
عائد (aa'id): A pronoun or element that connects a clause to its antecedent
وضع الظاهر موضع المضمر (wad' al-zahir mawdi' al-mudmar): A grammatical device where an explicit noun is used instead of a pronoun for emphasis or clarity
بلوغ (bulugh): To reach, made transitive with 'ila' by tadmeen, meaning 'to arrive'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many interpretations are given for the connector (al-rabita) in the phrase 'lam tablugh sifat tadqiqat'?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
A grammatical gap in an adjectival clause can be resolved either by an omitted pronoun or by the described noun itself acting as a connector through wad' al-zahir mawdi' al-mudmar.

The Rhetorical Use of Demonstrative Pronouns in Legal Texts
Explaining the use of a demonstrative pronoun for special distinction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a demonstrative pronoun (ism al-isharah) is used instead of a simple pronoun (damir) in classical Islamic legal texts and apply this understanding to interpret similar constructions.

Core Idea
Using a demonstrative pronoun instead of a simple pronoun signals special distinction and emphasis on the referent.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Tawdih examines a seemingly minor grammatical choice — why did the author say 'this book' instead of just 'it'? In legal texts, every word carries weight. The commentator reveals that this is not merely stylistic; it is a deliberate rhetorical device to bestow 'perfect distinction' on the work. Understanding such choices sharpens your ability to read classical usul texts with precision.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Linguistic Substitution
Recognize that the author placed a demonstrative (ism al-isharah: 'hadha') where a pronoun (damir: 'hu') would suffice. The base text says 'sammaytu hadha al-kitab' instead of 'sammaytuhu'.
2
Understand the Default Rule
In Arabic, when a referent is previously mentioned, a pronoun normally provides sufficient reference. This is the default, unmarked choice.
3
Grasp the Rhetorical Benefit
The commentator explains that the demonstrative adds 'complete care' (kamaal al-inayah) and 'perfect distinction' (kamaal tamyeez). The demonstrative draws attention more forcefully than a pronoun, emphasizing the uniqueness of the referent.
4
Apply the Principle
Look for similar constructions in other legal texts (e.g., 'hadha al-bab', 'hadha al-fasl'). Ask: Why might the author have chosen the demonstrative? What special significance is being highlighted?
This principle is part of the wider field of balaghah (rhetoric) often used in usul al-fiqh commentary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله سميت هذ الكتاب جواب لما وضع الاشارة موضع الضمير لكمال العناية بمتييزه فان قلت لما لثبوت الثاني لثبوت الاول فيقتضى سببية ماذكر بعد لما لتسمية الكتاب بالتوضيح فما وجهه قلت وجهه ان الضمير فى اتمامه للشرح المذكور الموصوف بانه شرح لمشكلات التنقيح وفتح لمغلقاته اتمام مثل هذا الشرح مع اشتماله على الامور المذكورة يصلح سببا لتسميت بالتوضيح في حل غوامض التنقيح. جواب لما سے بیان ترکیب ہے اسمیت جواب لما ہے۔ فائدہ ایہاں دو نسخے ہیں (۱) ایک نسخہ میں واؤ نہیں ہے اس نسخے کے مطابق ترکیب درست ہے سمیت جواب لما ہے (۲) نسخہ ثانیہ میں واؤ ہے دریں صورت و سمیت جعلتہ عراضتہ پر معطوف ہوگا اور جعلیہ عراضہ جواب لما ہوگا نہ کہ وسمیت۔ (۲) دوسرا جواب یہ دیا گیا ہے کہ واؤ زائدہ ہے عاطفہ نہیں ہے فلا اشکال وضع اسم الاشارہ الخ۔ جواب سوال سوال یہ ہوتا ہے کہ ہذا کتاب کا مشار الیہ کتاب ہے جو ماقبل میں مذکور ہو چکی ہے تو یہ موقع ضمیر کا تھا سمیہ کہنا چاہیے تھا اسم اشارہ ذکر کرنے میں کیا حکمت ہے۔ جواب حکمت یہ ہے کہ گو ضمیر کے ذکر سے مرجع کو تمیز حاصل ہو جاتا ہے لیکن کمال تمیز حاصل نہیں ہوتا جب کہ اسم اشارہ کو ذکر کرنے سے مشار الیہ میں کمال تمیز
His statement 'I named this book' is the answer to 'lamma'. He placed the demonstrative in the position of the pronoun for complete care to distinguish it. If you say: 'lamma' requires the existence of the second due to the existence of the first, so it necessitates that what is mentioned after 'lamma' is the cause for naming the book 'al-Tawdih'. So what is its aspect? I say: the pronoun in 'itmaamihi' refers to the mentioned commentary described as a commentary on the difficulties of al-Tanqih and an opener of its intricacies. The completion of such a commentary, along with its inclusion of the mentioned matters, is suitable as a cause for naming it 'al-Tawdih fi Hall Ghawamid al-Tanqih'. The answer is a structural explanation: 'sammaytu' is the answer of 'lamma'. Benefit: there are two versions. In one version there is no 'waw'; in that version the structure is correct: 'sammaytu' is the answer of 'lamma'. In the second version, there is a 'waw'; in that case 'wa sammaytu' is coordinated with 'ja'altuhu 'aradatan', and 'ja'altuhu 'aradatan' is the answer of 'lamma', not 'wa sammaytu'. The second answer is given: the 'waw' is extra, not a coordinating conjunction, so there is no problem. Regarding 'placing the demonstrative in the position of the pronoun': The question: 'hadha kitab' – the referent (mushar ilayhi) is the book which was already mentioned, so a pronoun would have been appropriate; why mention the demonstrative? The answer: the wisdom is that although a pronoun gives distinction to the referent, it does not give perfect distinction, whereas mentioning the demonstrative gives perfect distinction to the referent.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage addresses why the author of al-Tawdih used the demonstrative phrase 'this book' (hadha al-kitab) instead of simply 'it' in the sentence 'I named this book...'. The question is: since the book was already mentioned, a pronoun ('sammaytuhu') would suffice. The commentator explains that the demonstrative is used for extra care (kamaal al-inayah) in distinguishing this book from other works. Then the passage explains the grammatical structure of 'lamma' and its answer. It also notes a textual variant: some manuscripts have a conjunction 'waw' before 'sammaytu', which changes the structure. The preferred answer is that the 'waw' is extra. The final point is that using the demonstrative gives complete distinction (kamaal tamyeez) that a pronoun cannot provide. This is a stylistic choice for emphasis and clarity.

Key Terms
اسم الإشارة (ism al-isharah): Demonstrative pronoun, used here for emphasis and distinctiveness
وضع الإشارة موضع الضمير (wad' al-isharah mawdi' al-damir): Placing the demonstrative in the position of the pronoun for rhetorical purpose
لما (lamma): A conditional particle requiring an answer clause; here it links the completion of the commentary to the naming

D) Because he forgot to use a pronoun

Key Takeaway
In classical legal texts, using a demonstrative pronoun where a simple pronoun suffices is a deliberate rhetorical device to confer special distinction and emphasis on the referent.

The Particle 'Lammā' and Causality in Conditional Statements
Addressing objections regarding the use of 'lammā' as a conditional particle

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the particle 'lammā' in conditional statements and evaluate when the causal link between condition and result is necessary or can be relaxed using Hanafi usul principles.

Core Idea
Lammā requires a causal link, but Hanafi usul allows exceptions based on majority practice and context.

The particle 'lammā' is central to conditional statements in Arabic, often implying a cause-effect relationship. However, objections arise when the connection seems weak or absent. In this passage, the commentator addresses such objections with four nuanced answers, drawing on linguistic precision and Quranic usage. Let us examine how Hanafi usul handles these textual complexities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection
The objector claims that 'lammā' requires the condition to be the cause of the result, but in the author's phrasing, completing the explanation cannot be the cause for naming the book. Understand the specific challenge.
The objection hinges on the rule that 'lammā' establishes a second thing by means of a first.
2
Examine Answer 1: Specification of the Antecedent
The first answer refines the referent of the pronoun in 'itmāmuhu'—it is not any explanation, but the explanation described with specific attributes (such as 'sharḥ al-mushkilāt'). Thus its completion can validly cause naming.
This shows that context can specify the antecedent and restore causality.
3
Analyze Answer 2: Critique of Taftazānī and Quranic Evidence
The commentator criticizes Taftazānī's objection using Quranic example (2:5): Allah used 'ulā'ika' (demonstrative) instead of 'hum' (personal pronoun) to include attributes. This demonstrates that pronouns refer to essence alone, but demonstratives can include attributes, supporting the reply.
The verse is used to argue that the referent of 'itmāmuhu' can include attributes.
4
Evaluate Answer 3: Majority Principle
Causality is based on majority practice (ghālibī), not universality. The verse 'wa lammā tawajjaha…' shows that turning towards Madyan did not cause the statement; thus exceptions exist.
This relaxes the strict causality requirement for 'lammā'.
5
Assess Answer 4: Conjunction Analysis
The answer to 'lammā' is 'ja'altuhu 'araḍahu', not 'samaytuhu'; the latter is conjoined. The causal requirement applies only to the original answer, not to the conjunct. So the objection is misplaced.
This is a grammatical argument showing that the structure does not violate the rule.

حاصل ہو جاتا ہے گویا مشار الیہ محسوس و مبصر ہوتا ہے یہاں مقصود کمال تمیز کا حصول تھا اسی بناء پر اسم اشارہ ذکر کیا۔ جواب (۲) اسم اشارہ کو اس لیے ذکر کیا کہ مرجع بہت بعید ہو گیا تھا تو اسم اشارہ کا ذکر مناسب تھا ۔ فان قلت حاصل اشکال یہ ہے کہ لما موضوع ہے برائے ثبوت ثانی بسبب مثبوت اول اول جمله شرط ثانی جزاء ہوگا۔ ضابطہ مسلمہ ہے کہ شرط جزاء کیلئے سبب بنتی ہے جز مسبب بنتی ہے مثلا ان ضربت ضربی ضابطہ کے مطابق لما تیسرا اتمامه الخ شرط وسبب بنے گا اور سمیت خذ الكتاب بالتوضيح في حل غوامض الصفح جزاء اور مسبب بنے گا حالانکہ اتمام شرح الح توضیح نام رکھنے کا سبب نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ ان میں کوئی ربط نہیں ہے۔ جواب ! (۲) جواب وجزاء فقط سمیت ہے تو اتمام شرح تسمیہ هذا الکتاب کا سبب بن سکتا ہے یقینا۔ جواب ! (۳) سبیت و معیت بنا قانون اکثری ہے کلی نہیں ہے جیسے ۔ ولما توجہ تلقاء مدین قال عسی ربی ان بعد ینی میں توجہ الی مدین اس قول کا سبب نہیں ہے۔ جواب! It is obtained, as if the referent is perceived and observed. Here the purpose was to achieve complete distinction, therefore the demonstrative pronoun was mentioned. Answer (2): The demonstrative pronoun was mentioned because the antecedent had become very distant, so mentioning the demonstrative pronoun was appropriate. Now if you say: The summary of the objection is that 'lammā' is placed for the confirmation of a second thing by means of a first thing, so the first clause is the condition and the second is the result. It is an established rule that the condition becomes the cause for the result, and the result becomes the effect. For example, 'If you hit, I hit' according to the rule, 'lammā' then the third 'itmāmuhu' etc. would be condition and cause, and 'samaytu' 'Take the book with the clarification in solving the hidden aspects of the pages' would be the result and effect, whereas completing the explanation of 'al-Tawḍīḥ' cannot be the cause for naming because there is no connection between them. Answer (1): The referent of the pronoun in 'itmāmuhu' is 'sharḥ', but not absolutely, rather that description which is described with 'sharḥ al-mushkilāt wa fatḥ al-mughlaqāt' and other attributes. The completion of the description described with these mentioned attributes has the capacity to be the cause for naming 'al-Tawḍīḥ fī ḥall ghawāmiḍ al-...' so that the name matches the named. But the commentator Taftāzānī's answer is objectionable because the referent of a pronoun is only the essence, not essences with attributes. On this basis, Allah said in 'ulā'ika 'alā hudā' where He mentioned 'ulā'ika' the demonstrative pronoun and did not mention 'hum' the pronoun, because in that case the pronoun 'hum' would refer to the essences of the muttaqīn, while the Essence of Allah wanted to refer to the muttaqīn described with these attributes, so He mentioned the demonstrative pronoun. Answer (2): The answer and the result are only 'samaytu', so the completion of the description can certainly be the cause for the naming of this book. Answer (3): Causality and concomitance are based on a majority principle, not universal. For example, in 'wa lammā tawajjaha tilqā'a Madyana qāla 'asā rabbī an yahdiyanī' [28:22], the turning towards Madyan is not the cause for this statement. Answer (4): The answer to 'lammā' is 'ja'altuhu 'araḍahu', not 'samaytuhu', rather it is conjuncted. So it is necessary for the original answer to be the effect, but it is not necessary for the conjunct to be the effect, because the matters considered in the conjunct of the conjoined are not necessarily considered in the conjunct as well, just as with 'rabba', its object cannot be definite, but the conjunct of the object of 'rabba' can be definite. Ended the sermon of al-Tawḍīḥ with His help and grace.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is a detailed response to objections regarding the use of the particle 'lammā' in the author's introductory remarks. The objector argues that according to the rule, 'lammā' introduces a condition that causes a result, but the author's phrasing seems to violate causality. The commentator provides four answers. First, the pronoun in 'itmāmuhu' refers not to the absolute explanation (sharḥ) but to the explanation described with specific attributes, so its completion can be a valid cause for naming. Second, he criticizes Taftāzānī's objection by pointing to the Quranic usage where a demonstrative pronoun is used instead of a personal pronoun to refer to essences with attributes. Third, he notes that causality is based on majority practice, not absolute universality, citing the verse in Surah al-Qasas. Fourth, he argues that the answer to 'lammā' is actually the conjoined phrase, not the main verb, so the causal requirement only applies to the original answer, not the conjunct. This discussion illustrates the Hanafi usul methodology of analyzing textual constructions with precision.

Key Terms
لما (lammā): A conditional particle that establishes a second thing by means of a first thing, requiring a causal link between condition and result.
شرط (sharṭ): The condition clause in a conditional sentence; it serves as the cause (sabab) for the result.
جزاء (jazā’): The result clause in a conditional sentence; the effect caused by the condition.
سبب (sabab): That which necessitates a legal effect; here used in the linguistic sense of causing the result.
أولئك (ulā'ika): Demonstrative pronoun meaning 'those'; used in the Quranic example to refer to the muttaqīn with their attributes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul approach to 'lammā' recognizes that causality is a majority principle, not absolute, and textual analysis must consider context, specification, and grammatical structure.

Grammatical Analysis of Pronoun and Adjective in the Opening
Explaining the grammatical justifications for pronoun and adjective

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi linguistic justification for the use of a pronoun before its explicit referent and for the masculine adjective describing a broken plural in the opening of a legal text.

Core Idea
Pronoun before mention is valid when the referent is mentally present; adjective agreement flexes with linguistic nuance.

This passage from the commentary on al-Tawdih and al-Talwih tackles two subtle linguistic points in the author's opening: the use of the pronoun 'hu' before its referent 'Allah' is explicitly named, and the adjective 'al-tayyib' appears in masculine form while describing the plural noun 'al-kalim'. The commentator provides three answers to each objection, demonstrating the precision of Hanafi linguistic analysis as a foundation for usul al-fiqh. By working through this commentary, you will see how grammatical rules are applied and justified in the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two linguistic objections
Read the passage to find the two main issues: (1) use of pronoun before explicit mention of the referent, and (2) masculine adjective describing a broken plural. Understand why these are considered problematic based on standard Arabic grammar.
The objections are implicit in the 'Question' parts of the commentary.
2
Examine the first objection and the commentator's answer
The objection: pronoun 'hu' appears before its referent (Allah). The answer: the referent is mentally present, especially at the opening of a book. This is supported by Quranic examples where pronouns precede their referents.
The commentator distinguishes between explicit mention and implied/mental mention.
3
Examine the second objection and the three answers
The objection: 'al-tayyib' should be feminine singular 'al-tayyibah' to agree with 'al-kalim' (broken plural). Three answers are given: (1) 'al-kalim' is a genus, not a true plural; (2) 'al-tayyib' modifies an omitted noun; (3) Taftazani's rule allows masculine agreement when the plural has a 'ta'' al-farq'.
Each answer provides a different grammatical or linguistic justification.
4
Analyze Taftazani's rule (ta' al-farq)
Understand the rule: for plurals whose singular form adds a 'ta'' (e.g., kalimah -> kalim), the adjective can be masculine or feminine. Examples from Arabic illustrate this flexibility.
This rule is specific to certain broken plurals and is cited from the commentator Taftazani.
5
Connect to Hanafi usul methodology
These grammatical clarifications are not mere pedantry; they establish the linguistic precision necessary for interpreting sacred texts. A firm grasp of Arabic grammar is foundational for deriving legal rulings.
Hanafi usul places great emphasis on language (lughah) as a source of law.

شرح التوضيح والتلو
کے اصول وادلہ کی بنیاد کو مضبوط بنادیا اور احکام شریعت کے حواشی کو باریک بنادیا اور ان کے عمل کو دقیق و مشکل ترین بنا دیا ہر شخص کی وہاں تک رسائی نہیں ہو سکتی۔ (توضیح) افتح بالضمير قبل الذكر ليدل على حضوره في الذهن الخ. جواب سوال مقدر الیہ کی
ضمیر کا مرجع ذات باری ہے وہ مذکور فی ما بیل نہیں ہے اضمار قبل الذکر لازم آتا ہے؟ جواب! مرجع مذکور ہے کیونکہ مرجع کے مذکور ہونے کی دو صورتیں ہیں (1) کبھی مرجع صراحتہ مذکور ہوتا ہے (۲) کبھی ضمن حکما مذکور ہوتا ہے یہاں مرجع ضمنا و ذھنا مذکور ہے کیونکہ اللہ تعالی کی ذات ہر وقت حاضر فی قلب کل مئومن ہے خصوصاً جب افتتاح کتاب ہورہا ہے اس وقت تو حضور متیقن ہے اس کی دو مثالیں ذکر کیں و با الحق انزلناہ مرجع قرآن پاک مذکور فی ما قبل نہیں ہے (۲) انہ لقرآن، مرجع ماقبل میں نہیں بلکہ بعد میں مذکور ہے . وقولہ الطیب ۔ جواب سوال مقدر۔ سوال ! یہ ہوتا ہے الطیب الکلم کی صفت ہے الکلم جمع ہے: ضابطہ، ہے کہ جمع مکسر غیرذ والعقول کی صفت واحدہ مومنہ آتی ہے تو الطیبہ ہونا چاہئے تھا؟ جواب ! (۱) مذہب حق کے مطابق الكلم جنس ہے جمع نہیں ہے کما ھو رای الجمهور فلا امکال - جواب! (۲) الطیب الکلم کی صفت نہیں ہے بلکہ بعض محذوف کی صفت ہے جواب! (۳) شارح تفتازانی جواب دے رہے ہیں الکلم اگر چہ جمع ہے لیکن صفت کی تذکیر ایک ضابطہ کی بناء پر ہے : ضابطہ ، یہ ہے کہ ہر وہ جمع جس کے واحد اور اس کے درمیان تا فارق ہو اس کی صفت مذکر و مونث دونوں طریقہ پر لائی جاسکتی ہے مثال ل ذکر کی نخل خاویه ای ساقطہ یہاں صفت مونث ذکر کی گئی ہے اور نخل منقعر میں صفت مذکر ذکر کی گئی ہے اور مشکل ایسی جمع ہے اس کے واحد پر تاء داخل ہوتی ہے یقال نخلہ اس طرح حکم کا مفرد کلمہ ہے واحد پر تاء داخل ہے لہذا اس کی صفت دونوں طرح ذکر کی جاسکتی ہے۔
The Beautiful (1) Commentary on al-Tawdih and al-Talwih. He strengthened the foundations of principles and proofs and made the margins of the rulings of Sharia fine and made their practice precise and most difficult. Every person cannot reach there. (Tawdih) He opened with the pronoun before the mention to indicate its presence in the mind etc. Answer to an implied question: The referent of the pronoun is the Essence of God, but it is not mentioned in what precedes. Does there necessarily occur a pronoun before the mention? Answer: The referent is mentioned because the referent being mentioned has two forms: (1) sometimes the referent is explicitly mentioned, (2) sometimes it is impliedly and legally mentioned. Here the referent is impliedly and mentally mentioned because the Essence of God is always present in the heart of every believer, especially when opening the book, at that time presence is certain. Two examples were mentioned: 'Wa bi-l-haqqi anzalnahu' – referent is the Noble Quran not mentioned before; 'Innahu la-qur'an' – referent is not in what precedes but is mentioned afterwards. And His saying 'al-tayyib'. Answer to an implied question. Question: This would be that 'al-tayyib' is an adjective for 'al-kalim'. 'al-kalim' is plural. The rule is that the adjective for a broken plural of non-rational beings is feminine singular, so it should be 'al-tayyibah'. Answer: (1) According to the correct madhhab, 'al-kalim' is a genus, not plural, as is the view of the majority, so no problem. Answer: (2) 'al-tayyib' is not an adjective for 'al-kalim' but rather an adjective for something omitted. Answer: (3) The commentator Taftazani answers: although 'al-kalim' is plural, the masculinization of the adjective is based on a rule: every plural between whose singular and there is a separating ta (ta' al-farq), its adjective can be brought in both masculine and feminine ways. Example: 'nakhlun khawiyah' meaning falling – adjective feminine, and 'nakhlun munqa'ir' – adjective masculine. And 'masalih' is a plural whose singular has ta' entered. Likewise 'hukm' – its singular is 'kalimah' – ta' enters. Therefore its adjective can be mentioned in both ways.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is a grammatical and theological commentary on the opening words of the matn. The commentator addresses two linguistic issues: first, why the pronoun 'hu' appears before its referent is explicitly mentioned; second, why the adjective 'tayyib' is masculine while describing a plural noun 'kalim'. For the first issue, he explains that the referent (Allah) is mentally present, especially at the beginning of a book, so using the pronoun before explicit mention is justified. Two Qur'anic examples are given where pronouns precede their referents. For the second issue, three answers are provided: (1) 'kalim' is a genus, not a true plural; (2) 'tayyib' describes an omitted noun; (3) according to Taftazani, the rule that broken non-rational plurals take feminine singular adjectives is flexible when the plural involves a 'ta' al-farq' between the singular form. This analysis reflects the Hanafi commitment to precise linguistic reasoning as a foundation for usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
ضمير (damir): Pronoun, specifically referring to the subject (Allah) in the opening phrase.
مرجع (marji'): The referent or antecedent of a pronoun.
جمع مكسر (jam' mukassar): Broken plural, a plural form that changes the internal structure of the word.
تا فارق (ta' al-farq): The distinguishing ta' that marks the singular form of a plural, used as a criterion for adjective agreement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, why is the adjective 'al-tayyib' used in masculine form to describe 'al-kalim'?
A) Because 'al-kalim' is a proper noun and always takes masculine adjectives.
B) Because 'al-kalim' is a verb, not a noun.
C) Because of multiple justifications: 'al-kalim' is a genus, or the adjective modifies an omitted word, or a grammatical rule permits it.
D) Because the author made a grammatical error.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi linguistic reasoning uses context and mental presence to justify grammatical choices, reflecting the depth of their usul methodology.

The Pronoun Before Mention: The Rhetorical Opening of Al-Talwih
Sharh al-Talwih explains the rhetorical opening of the matn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the use of a pronoun before its reference (damir qabl al-dhikr) in a scholarly text, explain its rhetorical significance, and address the common objection regarding the basmala.

Core Idea
A pronoun before its reference signals immediate divine presence and is a deliberate rhetorical device, not an error.

The opening phrase of Al-Talwih, 'اليه يصعد' (to Him ascends), presents a striking rhetorical feature: the pronoun 'إليه' appears before its antecedent 'الله' is explicitly mentioned. This lesson unpacks the commentator's explanation of this device, its symbolic meaning, and the defense against the objection that the basmala should preclude such usage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rhetorical device
Locate the phrase 'اليه يصعد' and recognize that the pronoun 'إليه' refers to Allah, who is not yet mentioned. This is a 'damir qabl al-dhikr' (pronoun before mention). The commentator calls it an 'iqtibas' (subtle borrowing) from the Quran (35:10).
The device is intentional, not a grammatical error.
2
Understand its symbolic meaning
The pronoun signals that Allah's remembrance is ever-present in the believer's heart, especially when opening discourse on usul al-fiqh. It also indicates that Allah is the sole object of praise and attention.
The meaning is not merely grammatical but spiritual and pedagogical.
3
Analyze the potential objection
The objector says: if the matn begins with the basmala (which explicitly mentions Allah), then the pronoun is not before a reference; if it does not begin with the basmala, it violates the Sunnah. The objection assumes the basmala is an integral part of the book.
This is a classic scholastic dialectic (la yuqal... fa-innahu yuqal).
4
Examine the commentator's response
The commentator argues that the basmala may be recited orally or written for blessing without being part of the text. Thus, the pronoun before mention in the book remains valid. The Sunnah is upheld, and the rhetorical purpose is preserved.
This response rests on a distinction between the act of writing/reciting and the textual content.
5
Define key terms
The passage ends by defining 'al-su'ud' (ascending) literally as movement from below to above in place. This shows the commentator's precision.
This definition clarifies the physical metaphor used in the Quranic verse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله اليه يصعد افتتاح غريب و اقتباس لطيف اتى بالضمير قبل الذكر دلالة على حضور ذكر الله تعالى في قلب المو من لا سيما عند افتتاح الكلام في اصول الشرع واشارة الى ان الله تعالى متعين لتوجه المحامد اليه صول الشرع والهـ العطاء تعالى لا يفتقر الى التصريح بذكره ولا يذهب الوهم الى غيره اذله العظمة والجلال ومنها والنوال وايماء الى ان الشارع في العلوم الاسلامية ينبغي ان يكون مطمح نظره و مقصد همته جناب الحق تعالى وتقدس فيقتصر على طلب رضاه ولا يلتفت الى ماسواه لا يقال ان ابتدء المتن بالتسمية. فلا اضمار قبل الذكر وان لم يبتدء لزم ترك العمل بالسنة لانا نقول يكفى في العمل بالسته ان يذكر التسمية باللسان او يخطر بالبال او يكتب على قصد التبرك من غير ان يجعل جزء من الكتاب وعلى كل تقدير يلزم الاضمار قبل ذكر المرجع في الكتاب والصعود الحركة من الاسفل الى العالى مكانا
His saying: 'To Him ascends' - a strange opening and a subtle borrowing. He brought the pronoun before the mention, indicating the presence of the remembrance of Allah in the heart of the believer, especially when opening speech in the principles of the Sharia, and an indication that Allah is necessarily deserving of the direction of praises to Him, and that the Giver of Sharia does not need explicit mention of Him, nor does the mind go to other than Him because He is the possessor of greatness and majesty, and an allusion that the discussant in Islamic sciences should make the court of the Truth Most High the object of his sight and the purpose of his effort, so he restricts himself to seeking His pleasure and does not turn to other than Him. It cannot be said: 'If the text begins with the basmala, then there is no pronoun before mention; if it does not begin, then leaving the Sunnah is necessary.' For we say: It is sufficient in acting upon the Sunnah that the basmala be mentioned by tongue or occur in the mind or be written with the intention of seeking blessing without making it part of the book. In any case, the pronoun before the reference in the book is necessary. And 'al-su'ud' is the movement from below to above in place.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage from Sharh al-Talwih analyzes the opening phrase 'اليه يصعد' (to Him ascends) from the matn of al-Tawdih. It identifies this as a 'subtle borrowing' (iqtibas) perhaps from the Quran (35:10). The commentator notes that the pronoun 'إليه' (to Him) comes before the explicit mention of Allah, which rhetorically signals the constant presence of Allah in the heart of the believer, especially when discussing usul al-fiqh. This indicates that Allah is the only worthy object of praise and the ultimate goal of the scholar. The commentator then addresses a potential objection: if the text begins with the basmala (as is customary), then there is no pronoun before mention because 'Allah' is already mentioned. The response is that the basmala may not be considered part of the text itself; it is often recited orally or written for blessing. Thus, the pronoun before mention is still valid. Finally, 'al-su'ud' is defined literally as ascending from below to above in place, clarifying the physical concept of the term. This analysis highlights the Hanafi usul concern with deep linguistic and rhetorical precision in divine speech.

Key Terms
الضمير قبل الذكر (al-damir qabl al-dhikr): The pronoun that comes before the noun it refers to, as in 'إليه' before 'الله'.
الاقتباس (al-iqtibas): Borrowing a phrase from the Quran or hadith into speech; here the phrase 'اليه يصعد' is borrowed from Quran 35:10.
الصعود (al-su'ud): Movement from a lower place to a higher place, used literally for physical ascent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary on Al-Talwih, why does the author use the pronoun 'إليه' before explicitly mentioning Allah?
A) He made a grammatical mistake.
B) To indicate the constant presence of Allah in the heart of the believer.
C) Because the matn already mentioned Allah in the basmala.
D) To confuse the reader and demonstrate his linguistic skill.

Key Takeaway
The use of a pronoun before its reference in the opening of Al-Talwih is a deliberate rhetorical device signaling Allah's immediate presence and is defended by distinguishing the basmala from the text.

The Rhetorical Device of Idmar Qabl al-Dhikr and the Collective Noun 'Al-Kalim'
Commentary on matn opening: pronoun usage and word analysis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the rhetorical device of idmar qabl al-dhikr in a legal text and explain the grammatical status of 'al-kalim' as a collective singular with evidence from Quranic usage.

Core Idea
The matn’s opening uses idmar qabl al-dhikr to signal Allah's presence, and 'al-kalim' is a collective singular like 'al-tamr', not a plural.

In this lesson, we examine the commentator's analysis of the matn's opening. He explains why the author used a pronoun ('-hi') before explicitly mentioning Allah, and then clarifies the grammatical nature of the word 'الكلم' (speech/words). Understanding these linguistic nuances is essential for proper interpretation of legal texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rhetorical device
Recognize that the pronoun '-' in 'إليه' appears before its referent (Allah) is mentioned. This is idmar qabl al-dhikr, used to indicate the prominence of Allah in the believer's mind.
The commentator emphasizes this is deliberate, not a grammatical error.
2
Address the objection about Basmala
The commentator preempts the objection that if the matn began with Basmala, there would be no idmar. He responds that Basmala may be omitted or treated as separate from the text, so the idmar remains meaningful.
This shows the commentator's thoroughness in defending the matn author's style.
3
Analyze 'الكلم' as a collective singular
Examine the grammatical analogy: 'الكلم' is to 'الكلمة' as 'التمر' is to 'التمرة' – a singular noun denoting a collective genus. It is never used for a single word.
The word is morphologically singular (فعل) but semantically collective, leading some to mistakenly think it is a plural.
4
Examine Quranic evidence for gender flexibility
The commentator cites two verses (54:20 and 69:7) where 'أعجاز' (trunks) is described with both masculine ('منقعر') and feminine ('خاوية') adjectives. This shows that collective nouns can take either gender, supporting the claim that 'الكلم' can be described with masculine adjectives.
The evidence proves that gender agreement does not indicate number.
5
Conclude the correct grammatical status
Since 'فعل' is not a plural pattern, and the word never refers to a single item, 'الكلم' must be a singular collective. The masculine descriptor in 'الكلم الطيب' confirms this.
The correct view is that it is a singular collective, not a plural of 'كلمة'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله اليه يصعد افتتاح غريب و اقتباس لطيف اتى بالضمير قبل الذكر دلالة على حضور ذكر الله تعالى في قلب المو من لا سيما عند افتتاح الكلام في اصول الشرع واشارة الى ان الله تعالى متعين لتوجه المحامد اليه صول الشرع والهـ العطاء تعالى لا يفتقر الى التصريح بذكره ولا يذهب الوهم الى غيره اذله العظمة والجلال ومنها والنوال وايماء الى ان الشارع في العلوم الاسلامية ينبغي ان يكون مطمح نظره و مقصد همته جناب الحق تعالى وتقدس فيقتصر على طلب رضاه ولا يلتفت الى ماسواه لا يقال ان ابتدء المتن بالتسمية. فلا اضمار قبل الذكر وان لم يبتدء لزم ترك العمل بالسنة لانا نقول يكفى في العمل بالسته ان يذكر التسمية باللسان او يخطر بالبال او يكتب على قصد التبرك من غير ان يجعل جزء من الكتاب وعلى كل تقدير يلزم الاضمار قبل ذكر المرجع في الكتاب والصعود الحركة من الاسفل الى العالى مكانا جهة استعير للتوجه الى العالى قدرا و مرتبة والكلم من الكلمة بمنزلة التمر من التمرة يفرق بين الجنس وواحده بالتاء واللفظ مفرد الا انه كثيرا ما يسمى جمعاً نظر الى المعنى الجنسي ولا عتبار جانبى اللفظ والمعنى يجوز فى وصفه التذكيروا التانيث قال الله تعالى كانهم اعجاز نخل منقعر ای منقطع من مغارسه ساقط على وجه الارض وقال الله تعالى كا نهم اعجاز نخل خاوية اى متاكلة الاجواف ثم الكلم غلب على الكثير ولا يستعمل في الواحد البتة حتى تو هم بعضهم انها جمع كلمة وليس على حد تمر وتمرة الا ان الكلم الطيب بتذكير الوصف يدل على ما ذكرناه فسمع ان فعلاً ليس من ابنية الجمع فلا ينبغي ان يشك فى انه جمع كتمرو وركب وانه ليس بجمع كنسب ورتب ففى قوله والكلم ان كان جمعا خزازة لا يخفى والصواب وان كان بالواؤ.
His statement 'to Him ascends' is a strange opening and a subtle quotation. He brought the pronoun before the antecedent to indicate the presence of the remembrance of Allah in the heart of the believer, especially at the opening of speech in the principles of the Sharia, and an indication that Allah is necessarily the one towards whom praises are directed. ... And 'الكلم' (the word) in relation to 'الكلمة' is like 'التمر' (dates) in relation to 'التمرة' (a date); the difference between the genus and its unit is with the 'ta'. The word is singular, but it is often called a plural considering the generic meaning. Considering both aspects of word and meaning, it is permissible to use masculine or feminine descriptors. Allah said: 'as if they were trunks of palm trees uprooted' and Allah said: 'as if they were trunks of palm trees hollow'. Then 'الكلم' is used predominantly for many and is never used for a single one, so much so that some imagine it is a plural of 'كلمة', but not like 'تمر' and 'تمرة'. However, 'الكلم الطيب' with masculine descriptor indicates what we mentioned. So it is heard that 'فعل' is not among the patterns of plurals, so one should not doubt that it is a plural like 'تمر' and 'ركب', and not a plural like 'نسب' and 'رتب'. So in his statement 'والكلم', if it were a plural, it would be a specific form; the correct view is that it is with the waw.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) by the author on the opening words of the matn. The commentator explains why the matn author used a pronoun before mentioning the referent (Allah) at the beginning: it indicates that the remembrance of Allah is already present in the heart of the believer, especially when starting a discourse on the principles of Sharia. He then refutes a possible objection that if the matn began with the Basmala, there would be no need for such a pronoun; the reply is that the Basmala might be omitted or considered separate from the text. The discussion then shifts to the word 'الكلم', which is grammatically singular but often treated as plural due to its collective meaning. Like 'التمر' (dates, collective) vs 'التمرة' (a date), 'الكلم' is the generic noun. The commentator cites two Quranic verses to show that the word can take masculine or feminine adjectives. He clarifies that 'الكلم' is never used for a single entity, leading some to think it is a plural of 'كلمة', but it is not formed on the plural pattern. The correct view is that it is a singular collective, and its description with masculine adjectives (e.g., 'الكلم الطيب') supports this.

Key Terms
الكلم (al-kalim): A singular noun denoting a collective of words; not used for a single word, but treated as a gender noun like 'التمر'.
اضمار قبل الذكر (idmar qabl al-dhikr): The rhetorical device of using a pronoun before the noun it refers to, indicating the noun's prominence in the mind.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, why does the word 'الكلم' take both masculine and feminine descriptors?
A) Because it is a plural.
B) Because it is a singular collective and collective nouns can take both.
C) Because it is derived from 'كلمة'.
D) Because of the context of the verses.

Key Takeaway
The opening pronoun signals Allah's centrality, and 'الكلم' is a singular collective, not a plural, supported by Quranic usage.

Iqtibas in the Opening of Al-Tanqih: Rhetorical Device and Justification
Explaining iqtibas and its justifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the rhetorical device of iqtibas in the opening of Al-Tanqih and explain three reasons why the quotation is considered subtle (latif).

Core Idea
Iqtibas: making another's speech part of your own without citation, relying on its fame.

The opening of Sadr al-Shariah's Al-Tanqih is celebrated for its uniqueness. One of its key features is the use of iqtibas – a Quranic quotation woven into the author's words. In this lesson, we will dissect this rhetorical device, understand its definition, and explore why the specific quotation 'إليه يصعد الكلم الطيب' is considered especially subtle, adding layers of meaning that point to Allah's centrality.

Guided Path
1
Define Iqtibas
First, understand the terminological meaning of iqtibas: making another's speech (Quran, hadith, or poetry) a part of your own without citation, relying on its fame. The author uses this technique to borrow the Quranic phrase.
The word 'iqtibas' literally means taking a spark of fire; metaphorically, it illuminates one's speech.
2
Identify the Quranic Quotation
Find the phrase 'إليه يصعد الكلم الطيب' in the opening. It is taken from Quran 35:10. Recognize that the author does not cite the verse explicitly; he blends it into his own sentence.
The quotation is part of a longer verse: 'مَن كَانَ يُرِيدُ الْعِزَّةَ فَلِلَّـهِ الْعِزَّةُ جَمِيعًا ۚ إِلَيْهِ يَصْعَدُ الْكَلِمُ الطَّيِّبُ...'
3
Explain the Three Reasons for Its Subtlety
The commentator gives three reasons why the quotation is 'latif' (subtle): (1) it indicates Allah's presence in the believer's heart, (2) it shows that Allah alone deserves all praise, and (3) it points to the intention of the seeker of knowledge. Understand each justification.
These reasons connect the rhetorical choice to deeper theological aims.
4
Link to the Uniqueness of the Opening
The iqtibas contributes to the overall uniqueness of the opening. Note how the commentator lists this as the first excellence of the matn.
The author's style is considered novel and laden with meaning.

Source Text
